Wicked Game

by annadelamico

Summary

Millionaire hotelier Rio Vidal always gets what she wants.
This time she wants Agatha Harkness, former rich kid turned literature professor.
Only Agatha isn't going to make it easy for her.

Notes

hi everyone! hope you all enjoy!

Chapter 1

Rio Vidal always got what she wanted.

It was in her blood. Her father had always taught her nothing wasn’t impossible for a Vidal, to never accept anything less than the best, and she held that close to her chest.

Hence why she was arguing with someone from her marketing team before when she was set to head out for the evening.

“I said green. That isn’t green.”

“But turquoise tested better,” the marketing director insisted.

“I don’t care. Green is the brand. We’re sticking with that.”

“But…”

“Green. End of discussion.” She hung up the phone and gave Alice an apologetic smile. “Sorry.”

“No need to apologize,” Alice teased from where she sat on the edge of the bed. “I love seeing you in boss lady mode.”

Rio rolled her eyes. She had been friends with Alice for years, after meeting at a mutual friend’s yacht party. What the daughter of a rock legend and an hotel heiress had in common, she wasn’t sure, but they had hit it off immediately. Years later, Alice was a rockstar in her own right, while had become the owner of the Vidal Group, but they were just still as close as ever.

Which was why, when she received an invite to a charity benefit, she invited her for some good company.

“Who’s going to be there tonight?” Alice asked. “Anyone we know?”

“Probably.” Rio put her earrings in. “It’s a good tax write-off.”

“Surely some of them care about the kids?”

“I hope so.” Rio checked her reflection in the mirror. “I’m planning on donating a purpose-built playground. I have all the details sorted.”

“I thought it was going to be an auction?”’

“Yes. I plan to give then too.”

“So you’re really going for the charity? Not to network?”

“I don’t need to network,” Rio said dismissively. And she didn’t. No, a Vidal always stood on their own two feet, with nothing but their sharp instinct and a good woman holding them up. She only had the former, but it was enough to keep her upright.

“I always forget you’re stupid rich,” Alice admitted.

Rio didn’t like to think of herself as ‘stupid rich’. Perhaps she had the potential to be if her father hadn’t kept her on track. Most heiresses to billion-dollar hotel and business empires wouldn’t bother with education or concentrate on learning how to run the company rather than partying her adolescence away. She had been raised differently, though, and knew that generations of Vidals had worked hard to get her family to where she was now. Yes, she was lucky and lived comfortably, but she never took that for granted. Not for a second.

No, like her father, she hadn’t paid a single dollar without careful consideration. Her clothes were expensive because they made a good impression. Her cars were shiny and new because efficiency was the key to success. Maybe the yacht was a bit much, but it entertained her friends who offered her endless support. She was the last Vidal, after all. Her family thus became what she made it.

“I like to consider myself sensibly rich,” Rio corrected, making Alice laugh.

“You’re such a dork.”

“Shut up.”

“You are,” Alice insisted. “And I adore you for it, but maybe it’s time someone else did too.”

Rio sighed. “Not this again.”

“I just want to you to be happy,” Alice insisted.

“I am happy.”

“And in love,” Alice specified. “You’re amazing and deserve to find someone equally as awesome. Why don’t you just try going on some dates? You can’t hold out forever, and a little fun never hurt anyone.”

“So you’re happy in your current situationship?”

Alice blushed bright red. “It’s not a situationship. We just keep things casual.”

“Whatever. Look, you know what my father always told me. Every heir of the Vidal fortune has known exactly who they were going to marry the moment they saw them. My parents, my grandparents, my great grandparents, my great-great…”

“Okay, okay, I get it.” Alice got to her feet. “I just hope you’re not wasting your life on some family superstition.”

Rio smiled and cupped her friend’s cheeks. “I have a fantastic life, Alice. Even if I never meet her, I am more than satisfied with what I have. A comfortable lifestyle, a thriving enterprise, and friends I’d trade it all for.”

Alice smiled at the last part. “You are a big softie.”

Rio playfully swatted her butt with her clutch purse “Come on, we better go.”

“Let’s go enjoy ourselves,” Alice proclaimed. “And who knows, your future wife might be there tonight.”

Rio scoffed. “I doubt it. No one interesting ever turns up to these things.”

Agatha Harkness hated everyone.

Well, besides her godsons, and her friends, and she guessed her own godmother. Everyone else could go fuck themselves.

And so when she received an invitation to the benefit for the children’s foundation her godmother donated to, she wanted to rip it up immediately. There was nothing worse than putting on a smile, pretending she didn’t hate 98% of the guest list.

 She had tried to distance herself from that world. The world she had grown up in. Yet, every so often, she had to step back in. Had to become the oddity of the evening, and pretend she was naive to it.

At least she had been given two tickets. At least she would have an ally…an ally who cried off while Agatha was already on the way there.

“I’m sorry Agatha. Billy and Tommy have sickness bugs, and I think Vision has it now too.”

“You’ll be next then.”
“Wow, thanks for the encouraging words, Agatha,” Wanda huffed. “Can you cover my undergrad class tomorrow if I don’t make it?”

“What are you teaching?”

“Macbeth.”

“Again?”

“Sorry Shakespeare is too modern for you, Miss Greek Tragedy.”

“It’s ONE module. It’s not my fault the students love it so much.”

“You love it and don’t deny it. I know Sappho is your favourite poet.”

“Second favourite,” Agatha corrected. “Emily Dickinson has my heart.”

“Whatever. Please? You can do that why Lady Macbeth was in the right debate. That’ll keep them busy.”

Agatha smirked. Last time she did that, three students almost got suspended. It was totally worth it.

“Try have a good time,” Wanda encouraged. “Who knows? You might meet someone.”

Agatha scoffed. “Unlikely.”

“It will be with that attitude.”

“You don’t get it, Wanda. I hate the lot of them.”

“You don’t know half of them.”

“I hate them by association.”

“Just show your face and leave if you have to. Now, I’ve got to go. I think Tommy just threw up again.”

“Fine.”

“Enjoy the benefit.”

“Enjoy the vomit.”

Agatha put the phone down and scowled out of the window. This was going to be painful.

The benefit was bustling by the time she got there. Agatha grimaced as she walked in. The stench of wealth was overwhelming.

Everyone was dressed to the nines, making her best dress look pitiful in comparison. People stared at her as she entered, some looking her up and down, likely thinking she was someone who worked for the charity rather than an honoured guest. Others, however, stared at her knowingly, whispering amongst their friends as she walked through the room.

Agatha was tempted to get on a chair and announce herself to the room. ‘Yes, tis I! Agatha Harkness. The woman, the myth, the legend.  Feel free to take a photo as I’m never coming to one of these fucking things again.’

She didn’t though. Instead, she caught sight of her godmother and made a b-line straight towards her.

“Agatha!” Lilia approached her with open arms. She gave her a hug before kissing both her cheeks. “Oh my dear it’s been too long!”

It had been a few months since they’d seen each other. Lilia spent a lot of time in her Mediterranean homes these days, and Agatha liked to stay in New York. Her work at Westview University kept her busy most of the year, and she spent her breaks either helping Wanda with the kids, seeing plays with Kingo or heading up to Amherst to lend her expertise to the Emily Dickinson Museum. Not that it stopped Lilia from nagging her to come visit.

She knew her godmother wanted her to accept her hospitality. To step back into the world she had been born into. Yet Agatha had made the decision long ago that she needed to build her own world. One of old books and faculty meetings, and of people who respected her, rather than treated her like a scandalous oddity.

“I’m so glad you’re here!” Lilia grinned up at her. “Are you enjoying yourself?”

“I only just got here, but it looks like you’ve done a good job.”

“Yes, Stark Industries and F4 inc. have sent advance donations, and we have a lot of deep pockets here for the auction. We even have the head of the Vidal Group here. I think we’re going to have a huge total by the end of the night.”

“And you’re going to be known as the hostess of the mostess,” Agatha pointed out. She knew her godmother liked to make a splash.

“That too.” Lilia chuckled, then looked around. “Where’s your friend?”

“Ill,” Agatha answered. “Or about to be.”

“Oh that’s a shame. Well, at least that means you can socialise a little. Come over here with me.”

Lilia led her over to a group of people already in the middle of chattering. Agatha recognised one of them as the Van Dyne’s daughter, and the others as top businesswoman Eleanor Bishop, and Pepper Potts, wife of Tony Stark, who was absent that evening. She could tell because she couldn’t hear his voice; that man was too loud for her liking.

Eleanor looked her up and down. “Agatha. What a surprise. I thought you didn’t come to these things anymore?”

“I invited her,” Lilia said proudly. “You all remember each other, right?”

Eleanor and Pepper nodded stiffly, while little Van Dyne just looked confused.

Oblivious to the awkwardness, Lilia grinned and clapped her hands. “Very well. I’ll let you catch up!”

Agatha watched her leave, cursing that her mother had been so devious to give her a rich godmother (she was sure it had been part of a business deal) that actually fucking cared about her.

“So, Agatha,” Pepper spoke up. “How have you been? What are you up to?”

“Good, and I’m a professor,” Agatha answered. “Literature.”

Little Van Dyne seemed interested, and Pepper managed a smile, while Eleanor just scoffed.

“What university?”

“Westview,” Agatha answered.

Little Van Dyne grinned. “I went to Westview! In the science department, but still!”

Agatha managed to smile back. “Good to see a fellow witch.”

“Yep, go witches!” Little Van Dyne held out her hand. “I’m Hope.”

She shook the girl’s hand and offered a small smile. “Agatha. You’re Hank and Janet’s daughter, aren’t you?”

Hope nodded. “You know them?”

“Through my mother,” Agatha answered, and she spotted Eleanor smirk into her drink.

Eleanor had always been a jackass. A judgemental jackass at that. It seemed some things never changed.

Pepper stepped in to fill the silence one more. “So Agatha, are you…”

“You’re very brave,” Eleanor cut in. “Coming here tonight.”

Agatha folded her arms. “What’s that supposed to mean?”

“You haven’t been to an event in years,” Eleanor pointed out. “What, do you think enough time has passed that we won’t remember?”

“I have nothing to be ashamed of,” Agatha said with her head held high. “Never have, never will.”

Eleanor laughed bitterly. “I see you’re still keeping up that lie.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “And I see you’re still suffering from stupidity, Eleanor.”

Hope bit back a laugh, while Eleanor’s face went red.

“Stupidity? How dare you talk to me like that! Do you have any idea who I am?”

“Unfortunately.”

“You’re still the same, Harkness. All bark but no substance.”

“Ladies,” Pepper tried to interject, but Agatha couldn’t not have the last word.

“At least I don’t need Daddy’s money to make myself matter. Now, if you’ll excuse me, I want to look at the auction pieces.”

She turned to walk away, only to heard Bishop laugh.

“As if she can afford anything more than a bag of peanuts.”

Agatha wanted to turn around and slap that smug smile off that Bishop bitch’s face. But this was Lilia’s night, and she didn’t want to ruin it. So, with all her might, she bit her tongue and stormed off.

She made it halfway across the room before a firm body bumped into hers. Agatha caught herself from stumbling and quickly whirled to face whatever idiot got in her way.

Said idiot was a pretty brunette, wearing a simple black velvet dress and small hooped earrings. Likely a date of some wall street guy, or a company representative. Whoever she was, she stared back at her with big brown eyes wide and startled. In her irritable state, Agatha found it incredibly annoying.

“Watch where you’re going,” she snapped, before charging towards the bar. She needed a drink, probably two…or five.

 

Rio followed her to the bar, keeping her distance but always keeping her in sight. And what a sight she was. Beautiful brown draping over her one shoulder in loose curls, the small straps of her dress revealing an exquisite expanse of skin, along with the most teasing hint of cleavage. And her legs…it took everything for her not to stare. Yet what she wanted to see most was those piercing blue eyes, and to hear that voice again, rich and sharp. She wanted it all.

Pushing down her nerves, Rio walked confidently to the bar, saddling up beside her. “Hey.”

The woman looked up, her jaw quickly tightening. “If you’re here for an argument, I must warn you my bite is just as bad as my bark.”

Rio had a feeling that last part had nothing to do with her, and rather whatever had made her storm around the room at top speed. “No, I wanted to get you a drink.”

“It’s an open bar,” Agatha snapped.

“Not everything is free.” Rio waved down the bartender. “Two glasses of your finest. You know what.”

The bartender nodded and headed into the back, returning with a champagne bucket and two glasses. “Enjoy ladies.”

“Excellent,” Rio smiled. “Put it on my tab.”

The bartender nodded. Everyone knew she’d make good on it. A Vidal always paid their debts.

“What is that?”

“Bollinger.” Rio examined the bottle and nodded in approval. “Not a bad vintage for a commercial bar.”

She poured them both a glass, before pushing one across the bar to her compelling companion.

The woman stared at the glass, before picking it up and taking an experimental sip. Her eyebrows shot up. “Wow, that’s…that’s good champagne.”

Rio grinned and held out her hand. “I’m Rio.”

The woman looked her up and down with pursed lips before shaking her hand firmly. Rio relished the touch, so warm and soft. She swore she would worship those hands, along with the rest of her.

“Agatha.”

“Agatha,” Rio tasted the name on her tongue, and found it finer than champagne could ever be. “I like it.”

“You do?”

Rio nodded. “Apologies for walking into you. However I must admit, I’m glad I did.”

Agatha raised her eyebrows again. “You are?”

“I am. I hope this doesn’t sound too forward but I…I’ve been waiting to meet you for some time.”

Agatha stared at her for a moment before shooting her a deep glare. “Is this a joke or something?”

“What?” Rio frowned. “No, not at all. Why would you think I’d be joking?”

“Don’t lie,” Agatha sneered. “I know you all find it funny, but I don’t need some second-rate date playing silly games to win brownie points with their asshole friends.”

“What? Agatha I-”

“Just leave me alone.” Agatha went to leave, only to turn back and grab the champagne bottle, stomping off with it grasped at the neck.

Rio watched her go in awe. That wasn’t a woman. That was a certified goddess.

“Rio?” Alice’s voice came from behind her.

“Hey Al.” She sensed her move to stand beside her, but Rio couldn’t take her eyes off the sharp red merging into the crowd.

Alice must have followed her gaze. “Who was that?”

Rio smiled in wonder. “My future wife.”

-

Rio’s father had told her a story long ago. Of how by living generously and kindly, their family had been blessed with three gifts. The first was sharp minds, curious and contemplating. The second: hearts big enough to love and care about not only their inner circle, but anyone in need of their help and hospitality. The third was a more personal gift, a reward her father called it. The gift of knowing your soulmate at a single glance.

‘You’ll know, mi flor,’ he’d told her. ‘The moment you seem them, you’ll know.’

She trusted her father’s words, as she always had, but with age and experience, Rio wasn’t sure what that would feel like. How would she know for sure? Would she just have to take it with blind faith? Had it already happened? Had missed it because she wasn’t sure?

Then she saw her, and suddenly she understood.

“Rio, please just think about this,” Alice begged as she chased after her. “You don’t know her.”

Rio weaved through the crowd, desperate to find her again. That beautiful woman in the red dress.

Agatha.

The most beautiful name to go with the most compelling person she had ever met.

“Rio, stop.” Alice grasped her arm, making her stop. “Just take a minute, please!”

“I can’t, Alice. I’m telling you. She’s her!”

“Alright, but just think about this rationally, okay,” Alice pleaded. “She doesn’t know you. You can’t just bulldoze your way into her life. You need to get to know her first at least.”

Rio knew she was right, even if she hated it. “Fine.”

“Right, so what’s her name?”

“Agatha.”

“Agatha what?”

“No idea.”

“You’re declaring she’s the love of your life and you don’t know her last name?”

Rio nodded.

Alice sighed. “Alright, come with me.”

Rio followed Alice through the crowd to the auction lot table. There, she spotted the unmistakable figure of Jennifer Kale and stopped in her tracks.

“Why are you taking me to see your booty call?”

“She’s not my booty call,” Alice hissed, and Rio snickered.

“No, you’re hers.”

“Look, Jen knows everyone. We can ask her if she knows an Agatha here tonight.”

Suddenly, Rio was ahead of her. “Hey Jen.”

Jen turned to face them, dressed in an elegant evening gown that would have made Princess Diana jealous. “Rio, Alice. To what do I owe the pleasure?”

“Do you know someone here called Agatha?” Alice asked. “Brown hair, red dress…”

“Gorgeous,” Rio added, earning a look from her friend.

“I don’t know a…Wait, do you mean Agatha Harkness?”

Rio shrugged. “I didn’t catch a last name.”

“Was she snappy and kind of mean?”

“Yeah!” Rio grinned.

Jen sighed. “I know Agatha. She went to the same boarding school as me, but the year above. She was pretty infamous.”

“She was?” Rio wanted to know everything.

“She transferred during freshman year,” Jen explained. “The school went from middle school right up, but it wasn’t strange for people to just come for middle school or high school. I remember when she came though. It was chaos.”

“How so?” Rio pressed.

“Her mom died, and I guess the family estate sent her there to get her out of the way, which she wasn’t too happy about. She’d set fire to bins, throw things in the swimming pool, and who knows how many girls she got caught kissing in the cupboard at the back of the science lab. She almost got expelled three times, but she stayed for about a year before she left.”

“Why did she leave?”

“Her godmother took over custody. You know Lilia Calderu, right?”

Rio nodded. She had met her in passing a number of times.

“Well, she took her to Europe,” Jen explained. “Bounced around all these fancy schools before getting into Oxford.”

“So she’s smart,” Rio noted approvingly.

“Too smart,” Jen added. “She doesn’t have money. As far as I know, she was uninherited in her mom’s will, and Lilia paid for most of her education. Last I heard, she was a lit professor at Westview.”

Rio made mental notes of all of this.

“Is she married?” Alice asked, stealing a cautious glance Jen’s way. “Partner? Kids? Anything like that?”

Dread filled Rio’s stomach. That possibility hadn’t entered her head. Had the love of her life already met someone? Was she now forever cursed with wanting someone she could never have? To live alone forever. An hour ago, the thought of being a bachelor for life didn’t bother her. Now it made her want to cry.

“I don’t know,” Jen admitted. “She doesn’t socialise in our circles anymore. She’s only here because Lilia organised the benefit.”

“Will you speak to her?” Rio asked hopefully. “To find out if she’s…if she’s unattached?”

Jen’s eyes narrowed. “Really? Agatha?”

“Yep.”

Jen folded her warms. “What do I get out of this?”

“What do you want?” Rio was getting ready to give Jen one of her hotels she was that desperate.

“An invite on your yacht, preferably somewhere nice.”

Rio held out her hand. “Deal.”

Jen shook her hand before waving them off. “I’ll be back with the intel soon.”

Rio looked to Alice, catching her biting her lip as she watched Jen go.

“You’ve got it bad.”

“I know,” Alice said with a dramatic sigh. “At least my girl knows I exist though.”

“Hey, mine does too!”

“But does she know who you really are, Miss Vidal?” Alice questioned.

“Not yet,” Rio answered, though she was sure that would soon change.

 

Agatha had found a lonely table for her and her champagne and was enjoying her second glass when a familiar face came to ruin the ambiance.

“Agatha! It’s been so long!”

“Well, if it isn’t my least favourite vegetable,” Agatha sassed. “What do you want, Kale?”

Jennifer Kale sat down in the seat opposite her and picked up one of the wine glasses from the table. She helped herself to some of the champagne.

“Hey!”

“You didn’t buy it,” Jen argued. “It’s a thousand dollars a bottle.”

Agatha tried to hide her surprise by taking a long sip. “How do you know I didn’t splash out?”

“You’re on an academic’s salary, and the rest of the bar is free.”

Agatha didn’t understand why that Rio woman had wasted all that money on her, though she knew the type. Money was no matter so they just threw it around, while others scrapped for every last dollar. She herself had been lucky not to have gotten to that point, but living on her salary did not grant the luxuries of her childhood. The freedom she found, however, was priceless.

“So what’s new with you?” Jen asked. “Married? Kids?”

She couldn’t help but laugh. “Absolutely not.”

“Oh come on,” Jen pressed. “There must be someone.”

Agatha shook her head. “I like being on my own.”

“Right…still a lesbian then?”

Agatha folded her arms. “Are you coming on to me, Kale?”

“WHAT? No! I mean you’re very…I just…” Jen sighed. “Sorry. I’ll leave you alone.”

She went to go, but Agatha stopped her. “Wait.”

Jen froze.

“What’s going on? Is it some kind of game? You all buy me expensive drinks and ask me stupid questions to what? Laugh about me behind my back?!”

“No one is making fun of you,” Jen insisted. “You’re being paranoid.”

“Paranoid? Oh I’ll show you-”

“Agatha!”

She looked round to see Lilia rushing towards her. Jen seemed to take the opportunity and disappeared into the crowd, leaving Agatha even more frustrated than before.

“Agatha, thank goodness,” Lilia said when she reached her. “I have a huge favour to ask.”

She sighed. “What?”

“Nothing big! It’s just one of the special guests who agreed to part of the auction had to cancel. Traffic issues, apparently.”

“Okay…”

“I need you to take their place.”

She didn’t like the sound of that. “Doing what?”

“Well, you’ll come on stage, and we’d auction off…a meal with you.”

“No. Absolutely not.”

“Agatha…”

“You’re auctioning me off to go on a date with some rich prick!”

“I’ll win the bid,” Lilia promised. “We just need to fill the docket, okay? Everyone will be bidding on the yacht anyway. Please, dear. For me?”

Agatha tried to stay strong, but eventually she crumbled. “Fine, but I still don’t like it.”

“Thank you, my dear.” Lilia leaned up and kissed her cheek. “Now come with me. The auction is about to start!”

 

The auction was set to begin and Rio found her and Alice a table to one side. She looked over the auction brochure and made a mental note of where she could give. Most would be after the grand yacht at the end, but Rio was thinking more on the smaller side.

“I like the look of that Gibson,” Alice admitted, pointing to where the guitat was displayed at the side of the stage.”

“I’ll bid for you,” Rio suggested. “I plan on spending tonight.”

It was that moment Jen appeared, taking a seat beside Alice. “You guys got some good seats.”

“It’s strategic,” Rio told her. “Most people go for the middle, but it’s really the wings that offer the best experience.”

“Can you tell she’s a hotelier?” Alice asked Jen, who chuckled.

“Can’t knock her. I stayed in a Vidal Hotel when I went to Sydney. It was very impressive.”

“Oh I love that one!” Alice gasped. “The one with the giant fish tank?”

“That’s it!”

“They’re all rescue fish,” Alice explained. “Rio even built a sea-life rehabilitation unit on site. I told her she should convert some of the lobby into an aquarium, but she won’t listen to me.”

“I don’t need an aquarium,” Rio insisted. “The big tank is enough. Anyway, enough about the fish. Did you speak to Agatha?”

“I did,” Jen confirmed. “She totally thinks I’m trying to get into her pants, but she is indeed single.”

Rio couldn’t help but grin, but Jen held up her hand.

“Not so fast, Romeo. She’s also got it in her head that we’re messing with her.”

“What?” Rio frowned. “Why?”

“Because from what I’ve just heard, she had a bit of back forth with Eleanor Bishop which has set her on edge. Apparently, Bishop said she was too poor to bid on a pack of peanuts.”

Rio took a sip of her drink, clutching the glass so tight she was surprised it didn’t. How she couldn’t wait to wipe the floor with anyone who even looked sourly in Agatha’s direction.

The auction soon started, and as the dockets went on, Rio managed to get Alice the Gibson, and she scored herself some courtside WNBA season tickets. Her intention was to leave it at that, perhaps pick up anything if the bids were low so the charity got a bit more. Yet as things stood, she was more than satisfied with her haul for the evening, though she wasn’t completely happy.

She couldn’t see Agatha in the crowd. Not even the slightest glimpse of red. Rio hoped she hadn’t gone home. She couldn’t just find her only to have her disappear.

“Now,” the auctioneer began again. “Docket Number 12 has had a slight change from the brochure, but I’m sure you’ll all still be interested. A dinner for two at Le Bernardin tomorrow evening, all expenses paid. Only now you will have company of the lovely Agatha Harkness.”

Rio sat up in her seat and watched as Agatha stepped out onto the stage. Her body language was stiff, but she still looked breathtaking. She reached for her paddle, but Alice leaned over to stop her.

“Rio, you can’t buy a date with her.”

“Why not?”

“Because it would be fucking weird.”

Rio brought her hand back but still sat at attention.

“Without further ado,” the auctioneer continued, “I’ll start the bidding at $100.”

A paddle went up. “$200.”

“That’s Lilia,” Jen whispered. “I bet it’s a set up.”

“$200,” another voice called out, this time a man’s. Rio craned her neck to see, only to grimace. It was Ralph Bohner, Wall Street asshole.

“$300,” Lilia called out.

“$1,000,” Ralph countered.

“$1,500,” Lilia added.

Ralph stood from his seat this time, straightening his suit jacket before holding up his paddle. “$100,000.”

Rio looked to Agatha, who was signing something in Lilia’s direction. Eventually, the paddle went up.

“$100,500.”

Ralph laughed and held up his paddle again. “$250,000.”

“He really likes her, huh,” Alice commented.

“He always has,” Jen supplied. “He just doesn’t get the message. Now the poor girl is going to be stuck with that creep all night.”

Rio looked to Agatha, who was gesturing aggressively at Lilia, but no paddle went up.

“$250,000 going once,” the auctioneer called.

Rio looked at her paddle.

“Going twice!”

“Sorry Alice,” she whispered, before grabbing her paddle and jumping to her feet. “$45 million.”

A loud gasp circled the room as chairs shifted and heads turned, all wanting to take a look at the big bidder. Agatha looked to be in equal shock, her mouth hanging open comically. Rio found it adorable.

“Sorry,” the auctioneer spoke up. “Did you say forty-five million?”

“Yes,” Rio confirmed, looking to were Ralph Bohner still stood, shoulders slumped, and face filled with disappointment, “and I will go higher if Mr Bohner wishes to challenge.”

Ralph shot her a glare before dropping down in his seat.

“Forty-five million going once!”

No one challenged.

“Going twice.” The hammer came down. “Sold, to Miss Rio Vidal.”

“You’re a fucking idiot,” Alice told her, but Rio just winked and headed up to get her prize.

She shook the auctioneer’s hand and collected the documentation for the reservation, before moving to stand beside Agatha for a photograph.

“What was that?” Agatha asked under her breath as they smiled for the camera.

“I wasn’t going to let you go for dinner with that sleaze,” Rio answered. “And I do like the desserts at Le Bernardin.”

“Why did you bid that much though?” Agatha demanded. “The yacht isn’t even worth that.”

The photographer moved on, and Rio gently took Agatha’s hand. “The yacht is all well and good, but you, my love,” she placed a kiss to her knuckles, “are priceless.”

She walked back to her table, clutching the envelope in her hand while the warmth of Agatha’s skin still tingled her lips.

When she reached Alice and Jen, they both looked up at her with arms folded. Jen’s face was lightened with amusement, but Alice looked like she was going to bonk her on the head.

“What?” Rio asked as she dropped back into her seat. “It’s for the kids!”

Chapter 2

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for all the awesome comments! i'm hoping you wall enjoy this next part!

Rio got up as she did every morning. She woke up bright and early and headed to her workout room to do her usual morning miles on the treadmill, before taking a quick shower and making herself some breakfast.

Her New York penthouse took up an entire upper floor of a modern high-rise overlooking Central Park. Alice had asked why she didn’t just stay in one of her hotels. After all, she had two right there in Manhattan. Yet Rio had always liked to have her own space in places she visited often. Currently, she had a townhouse in London, a house in the south of France, smaller properties scattered across the Greek islands, and a summer villa on Lake Como. Most she had inherited, while others she had simply fallen in love with.

While her strikingly modern New York apartment was more for convenience than homeliness, she did enjoy standing by the windows with her morning coffee for some quiet moments of contemplation. Most of the time her mind was on work, friends, the general sorry state of the world. That morning however, there was only one thing on her mind. Something, or rather someone, who had consumed her entire being from the moment their eyes met.

Agatha Harkness.

Rio could help but smile at the thought of her. At her beautiful face, her sharp tongue, her smooth voice, those blue eyes that reminded her of a glistening ocean. She had always wondered what her future wife would be like, yet now she’d seen her, it could never have been anyone else.

Once her coffee was done, she headed to her bedroom. She pulled out the outfit she had already selected in her mind to wear that evening and laid it all out on the bed. It wasn’t too formal or too flirtatious but was smart and showed an effort had been made. The dinner was about getting to know each other, setting down the foundations of a friendship, or at least an acquaintanceship. After all, she was playing the long game.

As she changed into one of her business suits ready for a meeting uptown, her phone rang. When she saw the ID, she quickly answered and stuck it on speakerphone.

“Alice!” Rio greeted as she continued buttoning up her shirt. “How are you this beautiful morning?”

Her friend’s laughter filtered through the phone. “You’re in a good mood. Has it got anything to do with a certain reservation at Le Bernardin tonight?”

Rio grinned. “Perhaps.”

“I still can’t believe you did that. Why can’t you just ask a girl out on a date like a normal person?”

“It’s not a date,” Rio insisted. “It’s just dinner. I want things to grow between us naturally.”

“Yes, because nothing says ‘naturally’ like paying millions to go out with her.”

“For the last time, it was for charity!”

“Whatever. I just called to wish you good luck and just...keep it cool, okay? And don’t throw your money around. No expensive gifts or anything?”

“So no Cartier?”

“Rio...”

“I’m joking!” Kind of, anyway. “Thanks, though. I’ll call you when I get back.”

“Please do! This is the most interesting thing that’s happened to either of us in ages!”

“Are you saying we’re boring?”

“As boring as a hotelier and a rockstar can be.”

Once the call ended, Rio looked to her dinner outfit once more. This night was going to be one of the most important of her life, and she could hardly wait.

 

Agatha just wanted to get the entire day over with. Her morning classes had annoyed her, she had her office hour that afternoon which consisted of stupid questions, stupid ideas, and just general stupidity, and then she had that damn dinner with a woman who clearly had more money than sense.

At least Wanda had made it into work, so she had been saved from the hells of teaching Shakespeare. And she had someone sane to talk with at lunch.

“Vision took the boys to that diner even after I told him not too,” Wanda huffed as she jabbed her fork into her salad. “And hey presto- food poisoning!”

Agatha shook her head. “Well at least it taught him a lesson, but I do feel for the boys.”

“They seem okay now, but I kept them off school for the day. Vision wanted me to stay and help with them, but I knew if I did, I’d say something I’d regret.”

“He still on the couch?”

“Yep, and that’s where he’ll be staying.” Wanda then put on a smile. “So how did last night go?”

Agatha made a sound of disgust and Wanda chuckled. 

“That bad?”

“You wouldn’t believe it.”

“Tell me everything!”

Agatha sighed. “One of the dinner- date prizes at the auction cried off so Lilia made me take their place.”

“Oh God, what happened?”

“Lilia said she’d win me and we’d have a nice dinner, which I was fine with. And it was going well until Ralph Bohner started bidding away.”

Wanda’s eyes widened. “Is he the guy who wouldn’t stop sending you flowers?”

“And chocolate. And cheap jewellery. Anyway, he kept bidding and bidding, to the point Lilia couldn’t go any higher.”

“Oh no!” Wanda covered her mouth. “Please say you’re not going on a date with him!”

“Nope, because just as he was about to win, someone overtook him. So now, I’m having dinner with a millionaire tonight.”

“Shit.” Wanda leaned back in her seat. “So, you’re going out with some random guy?”

“Random woman,” Agatha corrected.

“Is she hot?”

“Wanda, that’s not the point. The point is that I’m going out for dinner with a complete stranger.”

“Isn’t that just like most first dates?”

“Woah, who’s going on a date?” Kingo slid down beside them in one of his usual dapper outfits, a fruit smoothie in his hand. “You know I don’t appreciate you gossiping without me, ladies.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but Wanda was all too happy to catch him up.

“Agatha has a date with a rich lady.”

“It’s not a date,” Agatha insisted. “It’s dinner. A dinner she won in a stupid charity auction at a stupid benefit run my stupid godmother who I’ll never speak to again.”

“That sounds like a meet cute if ever I heard one.” Kingo wiggled his eyebrows. “Is she hot?”

Agatha once again ignored the question.

“I’ll take that as a yes,” Kingo said with a grin. “So how much did she bid on you?”

“Forty-five,” Agatha answered.

Wanda’s eyes widened. “Thousand?”

Agatha shook her head. “Million.”

“Fuck!” Kingo gasped. “I mean…Agatha, that’s like…I’m lost for words.”

“And you don’t know this woman?” Wanda questioned. “At all?”

“No, I mean I spoke to her earlier in the night. She bought me a bottle of champagne, but I thought she was one of the gossipy wives trying to play a trick on me. I didn’t know she was rich rich.”

“She bought you champagne too?” Kingo snickered. “Oh, she likes you, Harkness.”

Agatha scowled and swatted his arm.

“Do you know her name?” Wanda asked.

“Rio Vidal,” Agatha answered with disgust. “Lilia has assured me she’s nice enough.”

“Rio Vidal?” Kingo questioned. “Like the Vidal hotels?”

“I guess?”

He quickly reached for his phone and tapped away at the screen. “It says here she’s the owner, chairmen and president of the Vidal Group, her family company.”

Wanda leaned over. “Are there any pictures?”

“Oh yeah,” Kingo grinned, showing her the screen.

“Agatha, she’s gorgeous!” Wanda gasped. “You have to date her!”

“I’m not dating anyone,” Agatha huffed. “Especially not a ridiculous heiress.”

“Yeah, yeah, yeah,” Kingo teased. “I bet you’ll be married by the end of summer.”

She shot him a glare and stole his smoothie. They were both foolishly wrong. She would make sure Rio Vidal left restaurant knowing she wasted her time and money, because Agatha was totally not interested.

 

Rio stood anxiously outside of the restaurant. Their reservation was at seven, but she had arrived twenty minutes early to make sure Agatha wasn’t waiting for her. Yet it was five minutes to seven, and her dinner companion was nowhere to be seen.

Had Agatha decided not to come? Had something happened? Was she okay?

She sucked in a sharp breath, trying to keep her worries at bay. This was fated somehow, and it would all work out. Like it had for every Vidal before her. Though none were likely as fiery and formidable as Agatha Harkness.

A cab pulled up and the passenger door flew opened, a familiar voice meeting her ears like a bird song. A very irritated bird song.

“…and if you think I’m leaving you a good review, you have another thing coming!”

Rio tried to supress the grin that pulled at her lips as Agatha appeared, dressed in yet another red dress. This one more casual, a summer dress that flowed lightly in the breeze, an oversized blazer covering up from the slight chill in the April air.

She watched her date slam the car door shut with a huff, before turning to face her. When their eyes met, she felt Agatha’s eyes pulling her apart. She had put on her best social wear: her leather pants, a maroon silk shirt with a grey blazer thrown over the top.

“Wow,” Agatha commented. “You almost look like a normal person.”

Rio chuckled. “And you look extraordinary. Now, shall we head inside?”

They headed in and handed the reservation documents to the hostess, who showed them to their table. Rio had always enjoyed the ambiance Le Bernardin, though it was never her place of choice. Though perhaps after this, it would become her favourite place in the world.

“Champagne for the table?” the hostess asked when they were seated, and Rio looked to Agatha questioningly, who shrugged.

“When in Rome?”

The hostess quickly returned with two glass flutes and a bottle on ice. Rio poured for them both, before joining Agatha in perusing the menu.

She was acutely aware they had barely spoken, not even small talk, and with every passing moment, it got harder to come up with something say. Eventually, she kicked herself enough to take the plunge.

“What are you thinking for your first course?”

“Caviar,” Agatha answered. “I don’t have it often, obviously.”

Rio nodded. She didn’t like caviar. Truthfully, she didn’t eat a lot of meats or fish. Her love for the natural world meant she loved every living thing, and she hated the thought of something suffering for the sake of her own pleasure. Hence why she didn’t like caviar.

“I’m thinking the salad.”

“Boring,” Agatha commented, and Rio couldn’t help but laugh.

“Guilty as charged.” She looked up at Agatha. “How was your day?”

“My day?” Agatha questioned. “Fine. How was yours?”

“Much better now,” Rio answered with a smile. “Jen told me you’re a professor.”

“Jen has a big mouth.” Agatha took a sip of her champagne. “I teach English.”

“Do you enjoy it?”

“I enjoy the research and the discussions. Sometimes it feels like a lot of it falls on deaf ears, but at least I have my postgraduate students to keep me sane.”

Rio nodded in understanding. “I ended up doing mostly business and science classes in college. Though I often ended up daydreaming instead of listening. I still do in boring meetings.”

Agatha gave her a tight smile before looking down at her menu again. Rio thought frantically for something else to say. Something to continue the conversation.

“What do you want for your second course?”

Agatha slammed her menu shut. “Okay, what’s going on?”

Rio blinked. “What do you mean?”

“Why are we here, Rio?” Agatha demanded. “Why did you bid that much on me?”

“Because I wanted to have dinner with you,” Rio answered without hesitation.

“Why? I’m not that special.”

The words stung Rio’s heart. “Of course you are.”

Agatha stared at her for a moment before shaking her head. “Whatever. It’s your money to waste.”

“I’m not wasting it,” Rio insisted. “Even if we just sit here in silence, I’d say it was worth it.”

“For the food?”

“I don’t really like seafood.”

“You don’t like seafood?”

Rio shook her head.

“Then why did you want to come here?”

Rio shrugged. “You’re here.”

Agatha looked deep in contemplation for a moment before eyeing her suspiciously. “So the bid was about me, not the dinner?”

Rio nodded. “I’d have paid the same to share a pizza at a hole in the wall.”

Agatha laughed and shook her head. “Wow. Okay.”

“Sorry.” Rio looked down at her lap. “Alice told me to play it cool, but I’m not good at that.”

She heard Agatha sigh. “Drink up, Vidal. Let’s go.”

Rio’s head shot up. “You’re going?”

“We’re going,” Agatha clarified. “You paid this much for my company, so let’s take my company elsewhere. Preferably somewhere that has proper portion sizes.”

“What about your caviar?”

Agatha shrugged. “I’ll get Lilia to buy me some. She owes me, after all.”

They downed their drinks, before standing to put on their coats. As she did, Rio spotted a couple in the corner of the restaurant, dressed in their best clothes and looking at the menu with lost expressions on their faces. She waved down one of the waiters and asked them to put the meal experience onto their tab instead, giving them a couple of hundreds for the trouble.

Once it was sorted, Rio held her arm out to Agatha with a bright smile. “What do you fancy, Miss Harkness?”

Agatha linked their arms together with a smirk “Now you mention it, I’d love a good pizza.”

Rio chucked as she led them out of the restaurant. “Your wish is my command, my lady.”

 

They found a little pizzeria a few blocks away, and Agatha had to say she was a little relieved. Here she would have equal footing, even if Rio was still the one paying.

Rio went up to the counter and ordered them a cheese pizza to share, before joining her back at their table. “Are you sure this is okay?”

“It’s fine,” Agatha insisted. “So, what’s the deal? Are you vegan or…”

Rio laughed softly. “No, I just prefer fish when they’re living.”

“Right.” Agatha knew rich people could be eccentric, her godmother was living proof, but Rio Vidal was something else. “Rio, this isn’t a date to you, is it?”

“No. Just dinner.”

Agatha relaxed. “Good, because I need tell you, I’m not interested in getting back into that old money scene again. I like my life the way it is, and I’m not uprooting it for anyone. No exceptions”

Rio frowned. “Anyone who asks you to do that clearly doesn’t care about you, Agatha.”

“So if we dated you would happily stay over in my one-bedroom apartment with crap air conditioning and a nice view of a side alley?”

“Why not?”

“Because you probably live in a luxury penthouse with a view to die for.”

Rio chuckled. “Okay guilty.”

“Have I disappointed you?”

“No.”

“Really?”

Rio nodded. “Who’s your favourite writer?”

Agatha blinked in surprise before answering.  “Emily Dickinson. I’m considered an expert on her, actually.” 

“Really?” Rio propped up her head with her hands. “Tell me more?”

Agatha waved her off. “You don’t want to hear all that. It’ll take us all night.”

Rio just smiled. “I have all the time in the world.”

They ate their pizza as Agatha talked, telling Rio of how she found Dickinson as a pre-teen and had memorized most of work by the time she was fifteen. How she had based her dissertation on her work during her last year at Oxford, and had explained her research, essays, and her work with the Emily Dickinson Museum.

Rio asked questions from time to time and laughed when she threw in a joke, but mostly she listened. Really listened. Like she was the most fascinating thing in the world. 

By the time they’d finished, it was getting late and the staff looked to be getting agitated. 

“My driver will pick us up,” Rio told her. “We’ll drop you back at your apartment.”

“I can get an Uber,” Agatha insisted, remembering she needed to give her ride there a one-star review. That ignorant jerk.

“I’d rather make sure you got home safe,” Rio insisted, and who was Agatha to refuse a free ride?

The free ride in question was a stylish black Range Rover, with smooth leather seats and that fresh new car smell still strong in the interior.  Rio helped Agatha into the back before sliding in next to her. “Hey Dave, can you take Agatha home first?”

“Sure thing, boss,” he replied, and Agatha quickly whittled off her address.

“That’s close to your campus,” Rio commented, and Agatha shrugged. 

“It’s convenient.” 

Rio nodded in agreement. “Can we meet up again? Maybe for coffee? Just coffee. As friends?”

Agatha wasn’t stupid. She knew Rio didn’t want to be just friends. Yet she had begrudgingly enjoyed her evening, and the thought of seeing her again wasn’t entirely horrible. 

“Maybe. I’m busy with classes and my research, so I’ll need to look at my schedule.”

“Can I have your number then?” Rio asked hopefully. “Or you can have mine. Whichever you prefer.”

Agatha bit back a smile. Rio’s eagerness was starting to grow on her. “Fine, but get ready because I’m only giving it once.”

Rio’s driver was very efficient and got her home pretty swiftly. She noticed Rio peering up at her building and wondered what it looked like in the eyes of a multi-millionaire.

“Thanks for dinner,” she quipped. “Hope it was worth the GDP of a small country.”

“It most definitely was,” Rio said with a grin. “I’d like it if I saw you for the price of a coffee next time though.”

Rio’s driver got out and opened the door for her, and Agatha was a little sad she had to go.

“Well, let’s talk about that coffee,” she said as she climbed out of the car. 

“Or just talk?” Rio asked. “You know, in general?”

“Goodnight Rio.”

“Goodnight Agatha.”

Rio’s driver shut the door between them and offered her a nod before climbing back into the front seat. She watched the car drive off, then headed up to her apartment

When she got inside, she flopped onto her couch and checked the notifications on her phone, finding one from Wanda.

WANDA

How was it?

She considered her answer before replying:

AGATHA

Interesting.

Wanda replied quickly. 

WANDA

Good interesting or bad interesting?

AGATHA

Just interesting. 

Then another message came through, one from an unrecognized number. 

so…coffee?

Then another came through.

this is rio btw

Agatha bit her lip, before saving the contact under RICH LOSER and setting her phone down on the couch beside her.

What the hell had she gotten herself into? 

Chapter 3: Chapter 3

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! sorry this has taken so long to update! hope you enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio was confused.

She’d thought the dinner went well and they’d been chatting back and forth over text ever since, but still Agatha wouldn’t go for a coffee with her.

Their conversations weren’t constant, she had to admit. Agatha would sometimes take a while to reply, but Rio understood she was busy. She on the other hand tried to respond as promptly as possible, pleased when she managed to catch her while she still had time to chat.

The conversations themselves were fun. Not too personal or too awkward (at least she didn’t think so). Their latest conversation had been about animals, which led to...

AGATHA

So you like spiders?

RIO

yes i have a tarantula called victoria

AGATHA

Where does she live?

RIO

currently she’s at my house in london. i get daily updates from my assistant.

AGATHA

When will you see her again?

RIO

i’m having her flown out next week.

AGATHA

All those carbon emissions for one little spider…so you’re staying in New York for a while then?

RIO

i didn’t intend to, but it seems i have a lot of business to take care of.

AGATHA

Business huh?

RIO

yes it’s making me particularly parched today…want to go join me for coffee?

AGATHA

Can’t. I’m making essays.

RIO

maybe another time?

  AGATHA

Yeah maybe.

Agatha never said no. That was the worst part. She just pushed it on to another time, and Rio held on to the hope that the next time she asked, it would be a definitive yes.

Work was a good distraction: they were in the process of buying a building in Rome, a former grand mansion that had been renovated into a hotel, only to fall into disrepair due to neglect and financial strain. Rio saw the potential and had a plan to return the hotel to its rightful grandeur.

They were set to close the sale by the end of the week, and her legal team were ready to submit plans and permissions to get the project running. She was excited, certainly, but it wasn’t with her usual ambition. No, she was excited because she could imagine visiting with Agatha. Perhaps she and Agatha could spend the summer at her villa and travel to Rome to oversee the project. Rio figured she’d have seen all the sights before, as she herself also had, but the thought of wandering the streets together eating gelatos before going to drink champagne on a rooftop balcony…oh she hoped to make that a reality.

In the meantime, she needed to work out how to get Agatha to agree to coffee, and blow off some steam. So she closed the VIP tennis court at her 5th Avenue hotel and called the one friend she knew would give her the challenge she needed.

“You’re good, Vidal,” Carol Danvers called across the court as Rio managed to score another point. “What’s that now?”

“4-5 to me,” Rio answered. “Need a breather?”

Carol shook her head. “Let’s finish this game first.”

They played on. Carol was a good player, though she hadn’t spent her childhood bouncing around luxury hotels. Rio was skilled at tennis, golf, swimming, diving, surfing, skiing, and she wasn’t too bad at basketball either. The prose of homeschooling and lots of downtime.

Carol had been born like her, with a silver spoon in her mouth, but had spat it out as soon as she was able. Her father died when she was a teenager, and she had sold off all the Danvers oil fields and casinos to focus on her true passion: aviation.  By 2035, Carol hoped to have a line of commercial jets powered solely by renewable and clean energy sources, a cause Rio was very supportive of. In the meantime, she was designing cars using similar methods, in the hopes it will encourage further development in the field.

As impressive as she was, however, it didn’t stop Rio from winning the game.

Carol chuckled as they walked to their water bottles. “So, I heard you bought yourself a date the other night?”

“I saved her from dating a douchebag,” Rio corrected, at which Carol gasped dramatically.

“Oh Rio, my white knight, how valiant you are!”

“It wasn’t like that,” Rio insisted. “She’s…you remember when I told you that story about my family. How everyone knows the person they’ll marry the moment they see them.”

Carol rolled her eyes. “Not that love at first sight bullshit again.”

“It’s not love at first sight,” Rio huffed. “Its like, I don’t know, everything clicks into place. You know why no one else ever stood a chance because it was always meant to be them, and now you know it could never be anyone else but them.”

“Right…” Carol wiped down her face with her towel. “That’s oddly specific…”

Rio nodded. “It is.”

Carol stared at her for a moment before her eyes widened. “Fuck off!”

Rio chuckled. “You’ve been spending too much time with Valkyrie.”

“No, no, we’re not talking about my messy love life! She’s your soulmate!”

“It’s not-”

“Stop, just let us talk about this, okay?” Carol grinned from ear to ear. “I can’t believe it actually happened!”

“Me neither,” Rio admitted. “I was starting to be a bit dubious of it all, but then I saw her and it’s like somehow this person I just met has become the entire centre of my life.”

“So you met her at the benefit?”

Rio told her the whole story. From bumping into each other, to the champagne, to the bidding war, to the dinner, and the conversations that followed. Carol, unable to contain herself, interrupted more times than she could count, but Rio didn’t mind. It was good to talk about it with someone other than Alice, who had told her twice in the last couple of days to stop being such a ‘simp’.

“Dude,” Carol said when the story was done. “You can’t fuck around with this. You gotta make a big gesture.”

“Like what?” Rio asked.

“Get her something nice like flowers or jewellery. Show her how serious you are.”

Rio considered it with a frown. “Wouldn’t that be a bit too forward?”

“You’ve got to let her know you mean business,” Carol insisted. “What do I always say? Higher, faster, further baby.”

Rio smirked and shook her head. Carol found any excuse to share her company moto- one she had come up with in Alice’s kitchen at 2am and never let go off.

“I’ll think about it,” she replied.

“Don’t think,” Carol pressed. “Just do.”

After a moment of consideration, Rio pulled out her phone. “I have an idea.”

Carol chuckled and patted her on the back. “Go get her, dude.”

 

Agatha loved her job. Sure, it wasn’t perfect, but getting to work analysing and researching something she was so passionate meant she could even look by the ridiculousness of some of her student’s work. She knew teaching a creative writing class would be a bad idea.

Just as she was reading yet another absurd and sickly love poem, there was a knock at her door. She looked over with a glare. “Come back during my office hours!”

A familiar voice followed. “Agatha?”

“Oh, Wanda.” She tossed the poem back onto the pile of papers before her. “Come in.”

Wanda entered, followed by a skinny boy in ripped jeans and a knitted jumper. His hair was black and curly, and he had eyeliner under his eyes, a look a lot of her students had sported during their ‘alternative’ phase. In his hands were a bouquet of purple roses, and a black giftbag.

“This young man was looking for you,” Wanda explained.

Agatha leaned back in her chair. “Are you in one of my classes?”

“No, I graduated last year,” the boy replied. “My boss sent me to give you these.”

She watched him place the flowers carefully on the desk, arranging them neatly along with the giftbag. Once he was done, he stepped back and nodded his head to her.

“She hopes you like them.” With that, the boy all but scurried out of the room, leaving Agatha with the mysterious delivery and her very nosey friend.

“Are these from Rio?” Wanda sat in the chair opposite her and appreciated the flowers. “Did you tell her you liked purple?”

“I did.” Over text, Agatha wanted to add. Rio couldn’t get brownie points for scrolling up through a text chain…right?

Though she had to admit, they were beautiful flowers.

Her attention however, gravitated to the little bag. She picked it up and looked inside, frowning when she saw another bag within it. She pulled on the string handles, revealing the little red bag, a familiar brand name written in gold on the sides.

“Cartier?!” Wanda gasped. “Isn’t the cheapest thing there like six hundred dollars?”

Agatha didn’t answer, instead she reached into the bag and pulled out the red jewellery box resting at the bottom. It was small, not ring-sized but it was easy enough for her to hold and open. Pulling up the lid, she found herself starting down at a simple gold band. She lifted it and turned it round in her hands. There were no stones encased in the gold, just a pattern of little circles with a line through each one. Along with it in the box was a small screwdriver.

Wanda reached over and picked up the tiny tool. “Oh I’ve seen these! You screw them on to fasten them.”

“I’m guessing its expensive?”

“They cost like thousands,” Wanda answered, before looking to the bouquet once more. “Hey, there’s a card in the flowers.”

Agatha dropped the bracelet back in the box and pulled the card from the bouquet. She ripped the envelope open and revealed the card within. On it was a single world.

Coffee?

Oh the nerve of that woman…

“What does it say?” Wanda asked, but Agatha ignored her, instead reaching for her phone.

AGATHA

You really are just another rich jackass aren’t you?

The reply came quickly.

RICH LOSER

did you not like the bracelet?

Unbelievable.

AGATHA

You can’t buy me Rio

RICH LOSER

i don’t want to buy you! i just want to go for coffee

AGATHA

Well I’m no longer interested!

Agatha discarded her phone and glared down at the bracelet.

“So are you going to return it?” Wanda asked, and Agatha laughed.

“Please. It’s Cartier. I’m not stupid.”

Wanda gave her a disapproving look.

“What?” Agatha questioned but her friend just shook her head.

“I think you’re looking a gift horse in the mouth.”

“Have you ever heard of the Trojan War?”

Wanda quickly got to her feet. “Nope. No more Ancient Greek stuff, please.”

Agatha chuckled as her friend quickly departed, before picking up the golden band once more. 

One thing she knew about Rio was that she had good taste. The rest? She wasn’t quite sure.

 

Rio cancelled the rest of her days meetings and shut herself in her office. She couldn’t bear to speak to anyone, let alone negotiate multi-million-dollar deals. Not when she had potentially ruined her entire future happiness because she was a fucking idiot.

That was the last time she was taking relationship advice from Carol Danvers. Not that she would need any more if she didn’t redeem herself to Agatha. The thought of losing her after finally finding her made a tear trickle down Rio’s cheek.

She leaned back into the black leather of her desk chair, and wondered how much money she would need to create a time machine for the simple purpose of hitting her past self over the head with a tennis racket and insist the flowers would do.

Cartier. What was she thinking?!

There was a knock at her office door. A five-beat rhythm that Rio knew anywhere. “Go away, Wu-Gulliver.”

The door pushed open, and Alice slipped inside. “What a lovely way to greet your best friend.”

Rio rolled her eyes in response. “What are you doing here?”

“Billy called me.”

Rio slumped further in her chair. If she was an asshole, she would fire him on the spot, but she knew the kid was only trying to help.

Alice sat on the edge of her desk. “So you bought her Cartier?”

“Yep.”

“Why the hell did you do that?”

“Well Carol said…”

“Ah.” Alice clicked her fingers. “That explains it.”

Rio sighed. “I know, I know.”

“I mean really, Rio? You take advice from the woman heading to her third divorce from the same woman?”

“At least she managed to get the girl in the first place,” Rio grumbled. “Look at me. I’m a successful hotelier. I’m meant to be a suave eligible bachelor but just thinking of Agatha makes me a fumbling idiot.”

“Your kind of always were a fumbling idiot,” Alice teased. “Look, you can fix this so easily by going and actually talking to her.”

Rio shook her head. “She won’t want to talk to me.”

“Fuck sake, Rio. If she’s ‘the one’ like you keep insisting, everything will work out and you can tell your little Vidal the same damn story your dad told you so he can go into this same ridiculous spiral. But even if she throws it all back in your face, isn’t it worth the risk?”

“Of course it is.” Rio sat up in her seat. “But I can’t just go down to the college and, like, talk to her though, can I?”

“As long as you don’t dance your way into her lecture singing ‘Can’t Take My Eyes Off You’,” Alice joked, before pointing a warning finger at her. “Or any other song, Rio. I’m fucking serious.”

“I promise. I’ll just talk to her.”

Alice grinned. “Good and never talk to Carol about this again. I love her to death, but her love life is a disaster.”

“Don’t worry,” Rio assured. “I’ll only be coming to you for advice for now on.

Alice’s smile faded. “Oh great.”

Rio arrived on campus within the hour and found her way to the English faculty building. Billy had warned her it was accessed by an ID card, and he’d been lucky to bump into someone who let him through. She, however, was not so lucky.

She pulled out her phone and was ready to text Agatha to come down when someone tapped her on the shoulder. Whirling round, she found herself faced with a tall man with a handsome smile.

“I had a feeling it was you,” he said with amusement. “You here to see Agatha?”

Rio frowned. Had Agatha been talking about her? “I am,” she answered, holding out her hand. “Rio Vidal.”

“Call me Kingo,” the man replied. “Does she know you’re coming?”

“Not exactly…”

Kingo chuckled. “In the doghouse already? Don’t worry. We’ve all been there. Last year she didn’t talk to me for a week because I spilt my coffee in front of her.”

Rio smirked amusingly. “She told me her bark is equally as bad as her bite.”

“She’s just trying to scare you,” Kingo assured. “Now come on, Romeo. I’ll walk you to her office.”

Kingo led her up to the second floor and brought her to a corridor lined with thick wooden doors, each one labelled with the name of their inhabitant.

“She’s third on the left,” Kingo told her. “Good luck.”

Rio gave him a thankful smile before walking towards the door in question. She smiled at the name plague: AGATHA HARKNESS, English Department. She wondered if it would look better with a little Vidal thrown in there too. That was thinking too far ahead though.

Coffee. Coffee was the goal.

And so, she knocked on the door.

“It’s not my office hour,” a voice replied. Rio sucked in a deep breath and pushed the door open.

Agatha was sat at her desk, looking down at a book. She looked beautiful, as always, but Rio couldn’t help but stare at the glasses perched on the end of that perfect nose. If she wasn’t already head over heels…

Agatha slammed book shut. “I said it’s not my…”

Their eyes met, and Rio noted the shock on the other woman’s face.

Agatha pulled off her glasses. “What are you doing here?”

Rio shut the office door behind her and walked further into the room. “I wanted to apologise. I see now that what I did was…I really wanted to get a coffee with you, and I got some bad advice. I should have, I don’t know, kept asking. I just didn’t know what to do.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “God, you such a loser.”

Rio nodded in agreement. “Pretty much.”

“I liked the flowers,” Agatha said, nodding to where they now sat in a clear vase on top of a small bookcase. “Cartier was just…”

“Too much.” Rio nodded in agreement. “I’m sorry. I’m not used to this kind of thing.”

“Asking a girl out for coffee?” Agatha questioned. “I find that hard to believe.”

“It’s true!” Rio insisted. “I-it’s a long story. But, if you’d still entertain me after all this, I was wondering if you’d like to go get a coffee? I’ll even let you pay for yourself if that makes you more comfortable.”

“Oh no. You’re buying, money bags.” Agatha checked her watch. “I have to set up for a seminar in half an hour. Will the campus coffee cart do?”

Rio couldn’t control her grin. “Coffee Cart sounds perfect.”

 

Agatha stood back and watched Rio as she ordered their coffees. Here was a woman who bought Cartier jewellery on a whim and could probably purchase the entire university without a second thought. A woman who had likely drunk the finest brews in the world served by people who had probably spent their life training to pour the perfect coffee. Yet there she was, chatting away to the undergrad working the cart like none of that mattered.

The girl at the cart was one of her students. Harper. She was one of the scholarship kids, and last summer she had stayed on campus to take extra classes. Agatha had assigned her a project to write a small collection of poetry in exchange for extra credit. It also gave her something to do when she wasn’t focusing on her work for the Emily Dickinson Museum. She saw a familiar fire in Harper, and a talent that needed nurturing.

Agatha decided to approach them and offered her student a smile. “Hi Harper.”

“Hi Professor,” Harper replied. “Your class this morning was really cool. I love the prompt you gave us. I’ve got some ideas already.”

“I expected nothing less,” Agatha replied, before looking to the two take-out cups on the counter. “Which ones mine?”

“This one.” Rio handed one of the cups over. “I made sure to keep track. I put three sugars in mine.”

Agatha grimaced at the thought.

“That’ll be seven dollars,” Harper declared, and Rio paid with her phone before fishing in her jacket pocket and handing over twenty dollars cash.

“Make sure you get yourself a coffee, okay?”

Harper grinned and pocketed the money. “Thanks, ma’am.”

Rio gave her a finger salute, before they both walked away to let the next person place their order.

“That was a generous tip,” Agatha noted, at which Rio shrugged.

“I’d have given her a fifty, but I didn’t want to be too flashy.”

Agatha had to admit she was glad Rio wasn’t throwing her money around campus, especially to her top student. “So, who’s this friend of yours who gave you that bad advice?”

“Carol,” Rio said with clear annoyance. “I should have known better. She’s one of the smartest people I know, but she’s currently on her third divorce in five years, so I should have probably known better.”

“So she’s had three wives?”

“No, just one,” Rio answered. “They remarried twice.”

“Why do they keep splitting up?”

“Well, the first time it was because Carol was always working, and I think the second time was somewhere along the same lines. This time, though, Carol called it quits.”

“How come?”

Rio shrugged. “She feels as though it just wasn’t working.”

Agatha couldn’t help but feel a bit sad for the sorry pair. “Will they get back together?”

“I don’t know. It’s different this time. Maria has gone and bought a house new New Orleans, and Carol has been spending a lot of time with our friend, Valkyrie. Alice and I think there’s something going on there.”

“Do you think that’ll end up serious?” Agatha hated that she was invested in this rich girl drama, though there was no messy like big money messy.

“No, I think they’re just hooking up,” Rio answered. “Valkyrie doesn’t do relationships, and Carol wants to rebound.”

“But won’t that be messy if they’re friends?”

“I don’t know. I’m keeping out of it.”

“Good idea,” Agatha chuckled. “So have you and Carol ever…”

“No way! We’re just friends.”

Agatha smirked. “Do you buy her Cartier too?”

“Only on special occasions,” Rio joked in return. Agatha laughed along with her, but she began to wonder…

“Rio?”

“Yes?”

“What do you want from me?”

Rio frowned, stopping in her tracks. “What do you mean?”

“Oh come on. This isn’t just about coffee. We both know you have an ulterior motive here.”

A guilt smile graced her lips. “Okay, I do.”

There it was. “Look, if you want to fuck me just…”

Rio’s eyes went comically wide. “What?! No! God no.”

Agatha put her free hand on her hip. “So you don’t want to sleep with me?”

“No, I mean yes, I mean…of course I do but not li-it’s not like that.” Rio looked down at her cup, a red flush on her cheeks.

“Then what is it?” Agatha questioned. “What do you want from this…courting ritual or whatever it is? Because I seriously don’t understand why you’re so-”

Rio looked up then, her fluster replaced with a conviction that sent a shiver down her spine. “I want to marry you.”

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat. Did she just…surely she didn’t mean it, did she?

“You want to marry me?”

Rio nodded. “I understand that we don’t know each other, and I don’t want to get married right now, but that is what I want in the end.”

Agatha stared at her in disbelief. This woman was fucking crazy. “Rio, this is the third time we’ve met in person.”

“I know, it’s just…” Rio bowed her head and stepped away. “I’ve messed up again, haven’t I?”

“I just don’t…”

Rio held up her free hand. “I’m gonna go. Thanks for the coffee.”

“You bought it,” Agatha reminded her. “And we haven’t even drank…”

“Have a good seminar, Agatha,” Rio said, before rushing off into the crowd of migrating students.

Agatha stayed stuck to the spot. Had that really just happened? Had Rio just proposed to her? No, proposed her intend to propose seemed more accurate. And then she’d run off, leaving the words stuck in the air like swinging swords.

She took a sip of the coffee and grimaced. Rio had given her the wrong cup, and she knew the sugary taste would linger in her mouth for the rest of the afternoon, along with the echoes of their conversation in her mind.

Chapter End Notes
