Chapter 4

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for all the comments and kudos! hope you enjoy this new update!

Agatha Harkness was a doomscroller.

Not in the traditional sense of hour and hours spent on TikTok or Instagram or whatever apps her students used instead of focusing on their studies. No, every night, Agatha would log onto her laptop and fall into an internet rabbit hole.

Most of the time it was to do with work, like a play Kingo would mention or a book Wanda suggest she read. That would then lead to her looking up something else, which would lead her to an article, then to an essay, until it was past midnight, and her eyes were straining at the screen even with her glasses on, swearing the next click would be the last.

That night, however, there was only one thing on her mind. And so, after settling into bed with her laptop laid on her stomach, she typed in two words:

Rio Vidal.

Most of the results were generic. Her Wiki page, her company website, posts from business and financial trades that made no sense to her. All pretty basic and boring. Until she found a Forbes article:

The Last Heiress: Inside the Life and Mind of the World’s Most Successful Hotelier.

Agatha clicked on the link, and a photograph of Rio all made up in a blue suit flashed before her eyes. Despite her oddness, there was no denying Rio was both beautiful and intriguing. She stared at the image a little too long, before forcing herself to scroll down to read the article itself.

Rio Vidal met me in the grand dining room of her 5th Avenue hotel. She had contacted my office a few days prior to ask what my favourite desserts were, and by the time we were sat down, an afternoon tea tray filled with my favourite cakes and confectionary was placed on the table beside us. I asked if this was a bribe, and she expressed her confusion.

“Isn’t it polite to ask guests what they like to eat?”

That’s when I realised Rio Vidal wasn’t going to be like any other interviewee I’d had be.

Agatha laughed to herself as she read on.

Ms Vidal was born in Delaware during a work trip that her parents tried to squeeze in before her arrival. However, their first and only child was eager to enter the world and was born in a community hospital a world away from the riches of her birthright. Despite admitting to have only visited the city twice (one of which being her birth), Vidal has since labelled herself a ‘Proud Delawarean’ and has openly joked about retiring there in her old age.

Agatha shook her head. There was no way in hell she was living in Delaware let alone dying there…not that Rio’s retirement plan would have anything to do with her. It was just a personal musing.

Yet Rio Vidal is very much in her prime, having inherited the Vidal empire after her father’s passing when she was just shy of twenty-one. Since then, she has doubled the company’s fleet of hotels and has further invested in technological, entertainment, and culinary enterprises. However, Vidal is no billionaire, though on paper she should be. Her large donations to charities, from multi-million dollar checks to purpose-built hospital wings and wildlife rehabilitation centres has kept her firmly under the billion-dollar line. In a 2022 interview with Time Magazine, Vidal explained her reasoning for this:

“I’ve never wasted a dollar in my life, and sometimes that means giving what I don’t need to those who do.”

Not wasting a dollar, huh? Agatha guessed the ridiculous donation had indeed been for the charity, a very deserving cause too. Though, even after Rio’s declaration that day on campus, she still didn’t understand why she did it. Or any of the bizarre situation they’d found themselves in.

She scrolled down to the interview section, skimming the questions about business until she found some that were more personal.

You have been labelled as ‘the Last Vidal’, making many question what the future of your family’s empire will have? Is that something you have already considered?

RV: (laughs) That’s a very morbid question. I will admit, I have thought about it. Of course I have. I’m hoping, however, that I will have children who will continue our family’s legacy. If not, then I will make the proper preparations to ensure the company remains in good hands.

And what of your love life? Usually, we see those in similar positions to yourself with a model on each arm, or married to a Miss Universe. When you could have your pick of the most beautiful, accomplished and intelligent women in the world, why have you decided to break the trend and stay single?

RV: Well, it’s about time that trend ended. I can guarantee most of those relationships and marriages are not based on love, but rather money and status. I have no interested in having a wife that I treat like a trophy while she in turn sees me as the living embodiment of an American Express card. I’d rather be alone forever than be stuck in a situation like that.

So you want real love?

RV: Doesn’t everyone? (laughs). I guess I’m a little old fashioned. My parents were soulmates, as were my grandparents, great-grandparents and so on and so forth. When I meet that person, I’ll be a lovestruck fool and will scream it from the rooftops. Until then, I have work to do.

Agatha bit her lip. Yes, that seemed like a very accurate description of her rela-acquaintanceship with Rio Vidal thus far. It seemed Rio had held on to this idea of a soulmate for a while. She herself had never subscribed to the idea, though she had often read about it. Studied it even. Her research into Emily Dickinson’s relationship with Susan Gilbert had pieced together a forbidden and sorrowful romance that would make Romeo and Juliet seem painless. She didn’t believe any two people were destined to be together though, especially if her person ended up being Rio fucking Vidal.  

She read that last paragraph again and again and again, before finally having enough willpower to shut her laptop down and turn off her lamp. Still, the words were etched in her mind, and she accepted that she’d be getting very little sleep that night.

 

Rio was miserable. Even more miserable than before. 

She had barely slept, hadn’t even attempted her usual round on the treadmill, and had Billy fetch her the greasiest, nastiest (but also vegetarian) breakfast burrito he could find when she made it to the office.

The burrito was a good distraction, and she had Billy send her the location of wherever he got it from for future reference, but once it was done, and she was stuck going through emails and paperwork, the thoughts quickly returned.

She had told Agatha she wanted to marry her. After only meeting her three times. Why had she thought that would be a good idea?

The answer was she didn’t think. She trusted her instincts like she always did, and while they were fine-tuned for business, they sucked when it came to anything else. Especially romance.

It was safe to say she had successfully driven away any chance of them spending any more time together, let alone the whole marriage and kids fantasy she had gotten herself carried away with. She wished she could explain it all to Agatha. About her family, her feels, all of it.

Instead, she had to just keep herself distracted until she found a way of getting on with her life somehow. Perhaps she should buy something for herself. A sports car? No. She had enough cars. A jet? Nope, bad for the environment. A new pet? No, Victoria would get jealous.

She was about to look up luxury apartments in Rome when there was a knock at the door and Billy entered.

Rio offered the boy a smile. After her last assistant moved up in the company, it had taken her six rounds of interviews to find the right replacement. Billy Kaplan was not the most qualified by any means, but she saw the potential and loved making a good investment for the future.

“Hey Billy, what's up?”

“Ms Calderu has come to thank you for your generous donation at the children’s benefit. Would you like me to pass on your regards?”

Rio frowned. Calderu? Why did that name sound- Her eyes widened. “She’s here right now?”

Billy nodded. “She’s stood by my desk. She’s brought a gift.”

“Very well. I’d like to accept it myself.”

“Really?”

Rio nodded eagerly. “Yes, send her right through.”

Once Billy left, Rio straightened up her desk and tidied her appearance, wishing she’d put on more than a white button up and slacks that morning. 

The door opened again, and Lilia Calderu walked in, dressed like an old-aged hippie, but Rio knew she was likely wearing a good $15K in jewellery around her neck and wrists. In her hands was a large bouquet of flowers. 

“Hello dear,” Lilia greeted her with a smile. “I wanted to drop these off personally to thank you for the most generous donation you made to the foundation. It alone was enough doubles what we expected to make for the night.”

“Anything for the children.” Rio took the bouquet and placed it on her desk. “Thank you for the flowers.”

“You’re very welcome, though they were something of a Trojan Horse to get me here.” Lilia gestured to the chair opposite Rio. “May I?”

“Please,” Rio insisted, and Lilia sat down, her elbows coming to rest on the desk.

“I wish to ask you something, Ms Vidal, and I would appreciate it if you answered honestly.”

“Of course,” Rio insisted. She wasn’t one to lie, and even if she was, she’d never lie to who would hopefully one day become her (god)mother in law.

Lilia stared her down. “What are your intentions with my goddaughter?”

“My intentions?”

“Yes, your intentions. Do you wish to be friends, or...”

“I wish to marry her.”

Lilia blinked at her. “You wish to what?”

“Marry her,” Rio confirmed. 

“But you hardly know each other.”

“I know but...”

“If this is about money, then...”

“No, it would never be about money,” Rio insisted. “Or anything so materialistic.”

“Then I simply do not understand. 

Rio could see why Lilia was confused, just as she understood why Agatha had been also. Yet she had promised to be honest, and so she continued to be so. “Will you allow me to explain?”

“I very much wish you would.”

She told Lilia her family’s story. Explained what she had been told as a young girl, and how she had grown up conflicted about its existence. Then she spoke of Agatha. Of how they literally bumped into each other, and how her world had spun off-axis ever since. To her credit, Lilia listened, waiting until she was done before speaking once more. 

“Does Agatha know this?”

“Just about the marriage part,” Rio replied.

“And what did she say?”

“Not much, but I could tell I had gotten ahead of myself.” 

“Perhaps if we lived in medieval times, your courting ritual would be very sweet,” Lilia noted. “Maybe some women would be swept up in it even now. My goddaughter, however, is not easily swayed. She’s stubborn, ignorant, and far too clever for her own good.”

Rio bowed her head. This wasn’t sounding promising.

“Yet she can be kind,” Lilia continued. “And sweet and soft and generous beyond belief. Perhaps try to get to know each other first. Talk to her about books and travelling and whatever it is you yourself enjoy. That may be the key to moving this forward.”

Rio nodded along, trying not to get her hopes up too much. Was this her receiving Lilia’s blessing?

“I don’t think she’ll want to talk to me after all this,” Rio admitted. “Not that I can blame her.”

“You leave Agatha to me,” Lilia insisted. “Just sit tight and keep it cool.”

Rio nodded in understanding, trying to push down the hope that had begun to blossom in her heart once more. If trusting Lilia was her only option, she would do so without hesitation.

After all, Agatha would always be worth the risk.

 

Agatha met her godmother for her standing afternoon tea reservation at The Palm Court. It was a sudden request, and from what she could tell by the older woman’s tone over the phone, one she could not refuse.

Lilia was already sat at the table when she arrived and stood to greet her with a kiss on each cheek. “My darling girl! I’m so glad you could make it.”

“Who am I to pass up free food?” Agatha said as she slumped into her chair. She reached for one of the delicate cakes on the silver stand and took a bite, moaning at the taste. God, that was good.

If her late mother was there, she would have been scolded for her lack of manners, but like always, Lilia laughed.

“You still eat like a teenager all these years later,” she teased, while pouring them both some tea. Soon, they started their usual chatter. Agatha updated Lilia about work, and her godmother paid her in kind with a farcical tale from her recent travels. This one involved a Sicilian donkey and a very angry crustacean.

After a while, however, Lilia’s expression gained a shadow of seriousness. “Now, I ‘m going to cut right to the chase. I didn’t bring you here to simply catch up, though you do know I love to see you.”

“Okay?” Agatha added some more milk to her tea. “What do you want to discuss?”

“Rio Vidal.”

The name shot through her like lightning, but she didn’t let it show. Agatha leaned back in her chair and folded her arms. “What about her?”

“I went to see her today,” Lilia admitted. “To give her some flowers thanking her for her generous donation at the benefit.”

Agatha could smell bullshit a mile off. “Oh really? That was your only reason for going?”

Lilia held up her hands. “Fine, I wanted to ask her what her intentions are with you, and as your legal guardian I have a right to ask.”

“I’m a grown adult,” Agatha reminded her. “I’m my own legal guardian.”

“I know, but I wanted to make sure Ms Vidal wasn’t just after getting you into bed.”

It would be simpler if that was the case, Agatha thought. At least then feelings wouldn’t be involved, and she would know how to handle the situation. She would have likely even accepted. After all, albeit strange, Rio Vidal was a beautiful woman, and she was due a little bit of fun. This, however, she had no idea what to do with.

“Did she tell you?” she asked, and her heart leaped when Lilia nodded.

“I was taken aback at first,” Lilia admitted. “Of course, I have heard of quick engagements and whirlwind marriages, but this is something else. Then, after she explained, I understood.”

Agatha frowned. “What do you mean explained? What did she say?”

Lilia took a sip of her tea before clasping her hands together on top of the table. “That’s an explanation Rio needs to give herself. And I urge you to ask for it with a matter of urgency.”

“What, are you Team Rio now?” Agatha sneered.

“She’s a good woman, and she cares about you,” Lilia argued. “Just hear her out.”

“You really think it’ll change things?”

“It’ll make you understand,” Lilia answered. “At least give yourself all the information before slamming the door shut.”

Agatha considered her godmother’s words before sighing in defeat. “Fine. I’ll talk with her.”

Lilia clapped her hands, a triumphant grin on her face. “Excellent! Now, I’m hosting a dinner on Friday, and I’d very much like you to attend. Just a few people, such as your friend, Alice and Miss Kale. You are very welcome to invite Ms Vidal as your plus one if you should so wish.”

“I doubt I will,” Agatha told her, though she was already wondering what dress to wear.

 

Rio had been in the middle of a zoom call with her legal team in Italy when her phone vibrated on the desk. She stole it a glance and saw Agatha’s name scrawled across the screen.

“Fellas, I need to take this call,” she told the team. “I will be right back.”

Muting her mic and switching off her camera, she scrambled to answer the call.

“Agatha?”

“Hey.” Her voice sounded thick like honey and Rio wanted to swim in its golden, sticky depths.

“H-how are you?”

“Good,” Agatha answered. “Just leaving a dinner date with Lilia.”

Ah. It seemed Lilia Calderu didn’t mess around.

“Did you both have a nice time?”

“We did,” Agatah confirmed. “Though we had an interesting conversation about you.”

“R-really?” Rio closed her eyes. Oh God what had Lilia said?!

“Yes, she told me that you explained this whole bizarre situation to her, and while I would like to argue how absurd it is that my godmother knows more about this than me, I too would like that explanation. So, I want to hear it.”

“What? Now?”

“Unless you’re too busy?”

Rio stole a glance at her zoom call, where her team continued to discuss the matter of city planning. “No, I have time.”

“Right, well, go on then.”

Rio sucked in a breath and told her the story her father had told her. Word for word. To her credit, Agatha kept surprisingly quiet, though after she was finished, the silence she was met with was near deafening.

“Well?” Rio asked cautiously. “What are your thoughts?”

“I think this whole thing sounds like the plot of a TV movie,” Agatha sassed. “However, I understand why you’ve got swept up in all this. And I’m flattered, Rio, I truly am, but I’m not the marrying kind. And even if I were, I don’t know you.”

“And I guess I don’t know you,” Rio reluctantly admitted, though in her heart it felt like Agatha had been there forever. “I’d like to, though. Know you, I mean. Even as friends, if that’s something you’d be interested in that is?”

There was a long pause, and Rio braced herself for a no, a never, the ominous beeps of a call ended. Though it seemed Agatha Harkness was full of surprises.

“Lilia is hosting an intimate dinner on Friday. Would you be my plus one? Not as a date, but as an…acquaintance.”

“An acquaintance,” Rio repeated with a grin. “I’ll be there.”

“Very good,” Agatha said sharply. “Well, I will see you then.”

“See you then.”

Agatha ended the call, but Rio didn’t mind. She allowed herself a moment to grin and kick her feet with excitement, before composing herself properly. Turning back on her mic and camera, she greeted her legal team with a smile.

“So, where were we?”

Chapter 5

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for the comments and kudos! hope you enjoy this new update!

Rio stared at the plans for the Rome hotel. The legal team had everything at hand and she had already begun speaking with architects and experts to preserve the building’s features. It was always important to her to keep a building’s character, especially a buidling in the historical part of one of the oldest cities in the world.

She wanted to get it right. No, needed to. No Vidal Hotel was the same, and from the heart of New York to the coast of New Zealand, each was created and managed with the upmost scrutiny and care. Yet Rio’s mind kept wandering, as it had done for days.

She had a serious case of Agatha Harkness on the brain.

Other days she had scolded herself. After all, she had a company to run. Yet for that day only, she allowed herself a free pass.

It was Friday. The night of Lilia’s dinner, and she was going as Agatha’s…acquaintance.

Her heart was practically bursting out of her chest. She just wanted to be there already, to be with her. Though she would just have to wait.

She decided to drop Agatha a text, in the hopes that would satisfy her impatience.

RIO

looking forward to tonight. do you want me to pick you up?

The reply came quickly.

AGATHA

As long as you don’t turn up in a horse-drawn carriage.

Rio smirked to herself.

RIO

damn i’d better cancel the marching band too…

AGATHA

I can’t tell if you’re joking…

RIO

guess you’ll have to wait and see.

AGATHA

Are you always this annoying?

Rio’s smirk transformed into a grin.

RIO

yep!

AGATHA

Great. Be at my place for six and don’t you dare be late. And stay by the car!

RIO

yes ma’am🫡 

Rio put down her phone and looked back at her work. It was difficult looking over the plans without actually being on the ground. She wanted to walk through the rooms, look out the windows, be able to feel the lifeforce of the building through the walls. A hotel to some were just a bed for the night, but to her it was more than that. It was an experience where dreams can be fulfilled, and happiness can be found. It was important every project went perfectly, and her usual hands-on approach would always ensure that.

Yet going to Rome would mean leaving New York. Leaving Agatha. It was silly, she knew. It would only be for a few days, but she still worried. What if Agatha suddenly decided she too was the one, and needed to see her in person that minute and she was stuck halfway across the world?

Also, Victoria was due to arrive over the weekend, and she was not fond of Trans-Atlantic flights.

She googled what the term dates for Westview University, and saw that classes stopped early May with graduation a few weeks after. Perhaps Agatha would have a more flexible schedule then? Maybe they could go together? As acquaintances, of course.

She shook the thought away. Nope. She was getting way too ahead of herself. They had dinner to get through first, and Rio needed it to be a good one.

 

Agatha had a problem. A big fucking problem.

It was her office hour, which was quieter than usual. The calm before the storm of finals week, she presumed. It meant, however, she had nothing to do but wait, and so she found herself on Google again, clicking the name at the top of her recent search list.

Rio Vidal.

It had happened a lot. First thing in a morning, last thing at night, while eating dinner and now, it seemed, while waiting for students to come tell her about their problems. She had officially entered a doomscroll rabbit hole she could not escape.

This time, she was on images. Most of them from business events or hotel openings. Nothing too exciting or scandalous, just fancy outfits in fancy places. Still, she couldn’t deny that Rio looked stunning in every single one of them. 

She scrolled through, admiring each stunning smile as she went, until one image made her pause. 

Rio was stood in a sound booth with a grin on her face, her hair tied back in a messy ponytail. She was wearing a tight black vest that framed her cleavage just right, while a thick silver chain rested around her neck. 

Agatha bit her lip. Okay, she looked really fucking hot.

She clicked on the link below, and found it was an article from last summer: an interview with Alice Wu-Gulliver. Rio’s friend from the benefit, who she would see with Jen at Lilia’s that evening. Agatha skimmed through the article, until she finally found what she was looking for.

Wu-Gulliver said having the hotelier be backing vocals on her song was “her favourite collaboration.”

“Rio was there when I wrote the song and helped me find the melody. It seemed only right she ended up on the record.”

Vidal is also a talented musician and had previously stepped up to help with the famous quarantine sessions during the Covid-19 pandemic. 

“We were quarantining together, and I wanted to do the album in my home studio, so Rio helped with drums and piano. It was a learning curve for both of us, but I think it turned out pretty good.”

When asked if she and Vidal were indeed just friends, she laughed. “She’s like my sister. My very strange and annoying sister. But whoever snaps her up will be a lucky lady. She has a heart of gold.”

Agatha was about to look more into these quarantine sessions when there was a knock at her door. She quickly shut the laptop and pushed herself back into reality. “Come in”

The door creaked open, and a familiar face appeared. “Hi Professor Harkness.”

“Harper, what a nice surprise! Please, come sit.”

Harper stepped across the room, dropping her tote bag to the side of the chair opposite her professor before sitting down. Agatha watched her eyes dart around as they always did, at all the pictures and bookshelves that covered her office walls, before she began rummaging through her bag.

“I wanted to ask about the  feedback you gave me for the poem assignment.”

Agatha frowned as Harper handed over the now crumpled paper, and read over her comments. It all seemed fair to her. “What seems to be the problem?”

“Everyone else got full pages of feedback and I just got a few annotations.”

“Yes?”

“I was wondering what I did wrong?”

Agatha’s frown deepened. “Wrong?”

“Yeah, because you didn’t give me feedback. Was it…is it bad or…”

“What? No, of course it wasn’t bad.”

Harper still remained confused. “Then why didn’t you give me that much feedback?”

Agatha smiled amusingly at the girl. She really had no clue. “Perhaps there isn’t much feedback is because I didn’t have much to give?”

“Oh.” Harper’s eyes widened with clear surprise. “Right.”

Agatha chuckled and handed the paper back. “You did well. Very well, indeed. I look forward to your next one.”

Haper took the paper and carefully folded it back in her bag. “Thanks, and sorry for wasting your time.”

“It’s fine,” Agatha assured. “How’s picking a major going?”

Harper shrugged. “Pretty good. I’m hoping to choose English.”

Agatha grinned. “I’d be disappointed if you didn’t.”

Harper offered her a bright smile, before getting to her feet. “Thank you for your time, professor.”

“Anytime,” Agatha assured, and watched the student leave. She wasn’t meant to have favourites, but she preferred Harper to the others in the class. For starters, she had a braincell, and she worked hard. An attribute she had great appreciation for.

Alone again, she opened her laptop once more. Agatha gave rockstar Rio one last glance before closing the tab. She needed to get a hold of herself. After all, she would be seeing enough of Rio that night, in her all strange and annoying glory.

She was definitely not looking forward to it.

 

Rio’s driver pulled up outside Agatha’s building ten minutes ahead of schedule. She had planned for bad traffic, but they had gotten there without much fuss.

Climbing out of the car, she straightened up her appearance. She had dressed in a simple black pants and blazer combo, with a low-cut black vest underneath. She knew people often went all out for these small, high society dinners, but that wasn’t her style. Even when she had a lady to impress.

Agatha must have seen her pull up, because before Rio could text her arrival, the brunette beauty emerged from the building. She couldn’t make out much of what Agatha was wearing under her coat, but the curls in her hair were more prominent than usual, and she wanted to tangle herself in them right there on the street.

“You’re early,” Agatha commented, and Rio nodded.

“Didn’t want to keep you waiting.”

She held the door open, and Agatha climbed into the car. Rio slid back in beside her and pulled the door shut.

Almost as soon as her driver set off, Agatha piped up again.

“Okay, an idiots guide to surviving Lilia’s dinner parties. Eat wherever she gives you, try follow the conversation because it can get a little out there sometimes, and don’t, under any circumstances, let Lilia do a psychic reading for you.”

“Lilia’s psychic?”

“No, but she thinks she is.”

Rio considered Agatha’s words before smiling. “You look amazing.”

Agatha bowed her head. “Thanks.”

“That’s something friends say, right?” Rio questioned. “I mean, ‘acquaintances’.”

“Do you say it to Alice?”

“I say she looks awesome,” Rio answered. “You know, in that rock and roll kind of way.”

Agatha sighed in defeat. “Fine, then I guess you look rather dapper yourself.”

Rio grinned the rest of the way there.

Lilia’s home was a stylish terrace mansion on the upper east side. Very flashy, very unique. Very Lilia. Agatha walked in like she owned the place, pulling off her coat to reveal a thin, navy knitted dress that hugged everything perfectly. It took everything in Rio not to stare.

The click of high heels echoed, and their host appeared from an adjoining room, dressing as outrageous as ever. Now Agatha had told her, Rio could see the psychic vibes.

“Welcome!” She greeted them both with a kiss on each cheek. “Come on through. The others are already here.”

To Rio’s relief, the others were indeed Alice and Jen. The former looking out of place (even at a fancy dinner, she dressed like a rockstar), while the latter, in their pink silk dress, looked very much at home. Lilia took her place at the top of the table, while Rio pulled out the chair beside her for Agatha to sit.

“Very gentlemanly,” Jen commented, and Rio noticed Agatha shot her a glare in response.

Rio sat beside her and smiled across at Alice, who simply raised her eyebrows.

It seemed Lilia had hired a chef and server for the evening. The server poured them all a glass of wine, before announcing the first course would be out shortly.

“So Rio,” Lilia began. “How are you?”

“Good. Happy to be here. Thank you for having me.”

“Well, it’s my pleasure,” Lilia stole a glance at Agatha. “I’m glad Agatha asked you to come.”

“Seeing as Jen invited her…friend, I thought I’d bring my own.”

Jen snorted. “So you two have the same kind of friendship as me and Alice?”

Agatha’s eyes widened for a moment before narrowing with anger. “You know what I meant.”

The first course soon arrived, while paused the conversation for a while. It was a creamy tomato soup, and Rio was relieved. Though she knew the next course would be a meat dish, she was glad it would only be one.

Once done, there were a few short conversations. Alice talked about her latest studio sessions, Jen shared some of the latest gossip in the ‘Rick bitch’ social circle, and Agatha criticized anything and everything. Lilia however, remained quiet, and Rio could feel her eyes fixed on her.

The next course was a vegetarian linguine. Rio frowned. She hadn’t told Lilia she didn’t eat meat, and when she looked to Alice questioningly, she simply shrugged. If Alice didn’t tell their host Rio preferred not to eat meat, there was only one other person who could have told her.

She smiled to herself as she tucked into the delicious meal.

“How’s work, Rio?” Alice asked. “Been busy?”

“Always.” Rio took a sip of her wine. “I’m finalizing the plans for the new hotel.”

“Oh?” Jen questioned. “Where abouts is this one?”

“Rome. It’s an old building, not far from the Pantheon. We’re working on removing the modern features, embracing the history while also granting the usual modern luxuries.”

“Do you have photos?” Lilia asked, and Rio pulled out her phone to show them. Jen and Lilia seemed impressed, while Agatha seemed mildly interested.

“Have you been yet?” Alice asked, and Rio shook her head. 

“No, I’m supervising from afar.”

Alice frowned. “You always watch over renovating a new hotel.”

Rio stole a glance at Agatha, who was watching her closely. “I have other stuff I need to deal with here. Also, Victoria is arriving tomorrow.”

Lilia frowned. “Victoria?” 

“My Tarantula”

“Her Tarantula.”

Rio looked to Agatha, who had distracted herself by stabbing at her spaghetti.

“Oh, you’re already in sync,” Jen teased, only for Alice to elbow her. “What? They are!”

Lilia cleared her throat. “When are planning to visit Rome then? In summer?”

“Potentially,” she answered. “We’ll see.”

She noticed Agatha glance her way, but the moment their eyes met she looked away again. 

“I have a villa in Sicily,” Lilia told her. “Why don’t we have a girl’s trip?”

Jen shot up in her seat. “That sounds perfect. We can fly to Rome for a few days. Rio can work while we shop!”

“Rio also has a place on Lake Como,” Alice helpfully supplied. “We could go there too.”

Lilia clapped her hands. “That’s settled then. What dates are everyone available?”

“I have none,” Agatha told them firmly. “Some of us have actual jobs besides being rich.”

“Hey, I have a job,” Alice argued, at which Agatha shrugged.

“Debatable, but fine.”

“You must be going on summer break soon though,” Jen commented. “Don’t colleges break off in like, what? Mid-May?”

“It’s not a break for professors,” Agatha reminded her. “I still need to work.”

“You can work pool-side,” Lilia told her. “It’ll be good for you to get a little sun.”

“Oh yes. Sunburn. Fun.”

Rio bit her lip as not to laugh.

“Don’t be a smartass,” Lilia snapped. “We’ll send each other our availability and go from there. It’ll be fun, and maybe…enlightening.”

Agatha caught Rio’s eye before stabbing her fork through the spaghetti once more.
Rio took that as she’ll think about it.

 

Agatha refused to speak all the way through dessert. Jen had tried to bait her, Lilia had asked her questions, and Alice had an annoying tendency to make sure she was okay. She ignored them, devouring the chocolate fudge cake before stealing what Rio had left over. It may not have been good for her, but it made her feel better at least. She really wanted to leave.

In the end, it was Rio to the rescue.

“I thank you for your hospitality,” she said to Lilia as she got to her feet, “but I have a business call with Rome at 4AM, and I need at least a few hours’ sleep.”

“Of course.” Lilia went to stand, but Rio held up a hand to stop her.

“Please, stay and enjoy your evening, though I will have to steal your niece. I didn’t promise to get her home safe.”

“Who did you promise?” Jen questioned, and Agatha wondered the same.

“Myself,” Rio answered. “And I always keep my promises.”

Agatha dabbed her lips with a napkin, before standing also. “Well, ladies. I’d say it’s been a pleasure, but I’d be lying.”

Lilia simply rolled her eyes. “Goodbye Agatha.”

Agatha gave her godmother a petty wave before leading Rio out of the dining room. She grabbed her coat and shrugged it on.

“Is your car here?”

“It’s been here the whole time,” Rio explained. “My driver is binge-watching Married at First Sight Australia.”

“Does anything normal ever come out of your mouth?” Agatha asked as they exited the mansion.

Rio smirked with amusement. “I guess you’ll have to see.”

Once in the safety of the car, Rio asked the question Agatha had been dreading. “Are you alright?”

“I’m fine,” she assured. “Always am.”

“Just ignore the Rome stuff,” Rio told her. “You’re a busy woman. You don’t have time to be galivanting all over Italy.”

“Neither do you,” Agatha argued. “But you didn’t argue.”

“Well, it would be a business trip for me,” Rio reminded her. “Sandwiched by a bit of leisure.”

Agatha tilted her head. “So not pleasure?”

Rio chuckled. “You know the answer to that.”

Agatha bit her lip and looked down at her lap. “Rio?”

“Yes?”

“I know you want more from me than this, and I appreciate you stepping back.”

“Hey, I’ll do whatever you want,” Rio insisted. “All you have to do is ask.”

Agatha nodded in understanding. “So if I did want you to marry me, which is not what I’m asking so don’t get excited, I’d just have to ask?”

“Ask me to ask you,” Rio corrected. “I want to propose.”

Agatha eyed her suspiciously. “You have a ring, don’t you.”

“No, I don’t.”

“Honestly?”

Rio held up her hands. “I swear. No ring has been purchased.”

“Right, well, I’m glad we are in agreement.”

“Me too.” Rio smiled at her, and Agatha’s heart skipped at the sight.

Nope, nope. Absolutely not!

Agatha pursed her lips. “So, how big is the carbon footprint of your stupid tarantula?”

They chatted casually the rest of the way home, and Agatha promise to call Rio at some point that week. Rio remained giddy, and she played it cool in response. Or cold. Sometimes she didn’t know the difference.

It was an hour or so later, when she was in her pyjamas and laid in bed, that her mind wandered into dangerous territory once more. Picking up her laptop, she typed in those two words again.

Rio Vidal.

This time, she went on videos. Most of them were of hotel grand openings and short interviews at events. All entertaining enough, especially when Rio got a little flustered or said something dorky, but nothing that was too captivating. That was until she found one that immediately spiked her interest. It was a recording of a conference speech regarding the safety of Marine life off the Australia coast.

Rio stood at a podium, dressed in a grey pant suit, reading from the prepared speech before her.

“There is no doubt that Australia is home to some of the world’s most spectacular wonders of the natural world. One of which being the Great Barrier Reef. A place of outstanding natural beauty, a hive of marine life, and most importantly the setting for Finding Nemo. (Laughter). Yet the Great Barrier Reef is dying, as are other habitats for marine life along the Australian coastline. And that’s all down to us. Human beings. How? Well, by being careless. That’s the basics of it. We’re a careless species, a selfish species, and it was about time…”

Agatha closed her eyes, listening to her go on and on about fucking fish. God, there was something about her voice. She hadn’t noticed it before, but it was so smooth, so thick. She wanted to wrap herself in it and never leave.

She recalled the way Rio said her name, how she complimented her, how she praised her like she was the best thing to ever exist. She bit her lip hard. Although she’d deny it until her last breath, it made her feel so fucking good.

Her hand began to slip down her stomach to the waistband of her sleep shorts, slipping under until she found…

Agatha shot up and slammed her laptop shut.

No, no, no. She wasn’t doing this. Absolutely not. Never, ever in a million years.

Switching off her light, she curled up against the pillows and clenched her eyes shut.

It was nothing more than a moment of weakness, she told herself. One she swore would never, ever happen again.

Ever.

“So let me get this straight. You got the chance to villa hop around Italy and you refused?!”

Agatha sighed. She should have just said the dinner went fine, but no. She had to fucking complain and yap herself into a corner. Now, her entire lunch break was being taken up by this ridiculous interrogation.

“I don’t want to live that lifestyle anymore,” she explained, but her friend wasn’t convinced.

“You’re not ‘living that lifestyle’. You’re going on vacation with your friends.”

“They’re not my friends,” Agatha insisted. “Lilia is my godmother, Jen is just someone I know from school, I hardly know Alice, and Rio is…well, Rio.”

“Yes, Rio is definitely Rio,” Wanda teased. “How’s that going, by the way?”

“We’re talking,” Agatha shrugged. “It’s nothing really.”

“But you said she wants to marry you?”

“I know, but she’s respecting my boundaries.”

“So, you told her you don’t want to marry her?”

“I told her I’ll tell her if I ever want to marry her.”

“Seriously?”

“What?”

“I tolerate her.”

“But do you have any feelings towards her?”

“Not particularly,” Agatha lied. She didn’t have romantic feelings, that was certain. Lustful feelings? Well, they had crept up on her unexpectedly, and she had promptly pushed them away. She had also stopped looking up Rio online, though she had spent most of her morning class thinking about one particular photo she’d seen that captured her arm muscles just right…

They had a few conflicts of opinion, though. Agatha was not interested in sports and found them ridiculous, while Rio was very active, both physically and supportively, in many sports. Yet when Agatha pointed out she probably had a half a rainforest worth of books in her apartment, Rio had been more intrigued than scandalised.

“I’m dismissing it because it is indeed nothing,” Agatha insisted. “And anyway, I have a young literary genius to mentor. Did you read the poem I sent you?”

I was talking to her after class yesterday and she said they are kicking her out of dorms for the summer, and the coffee cart is closing while the campus is quiet. I told her I would keep an ear out for any cheap rentals, and I think she’s looking for some waitressing gigs.”

That one place that would have defined her childhood, where most days were the same and she had school, and steady friends, and hobbies beyond what a hotel complex could offer. If she were to have children with Agatha, she knew education would be important, and that they would need to have a base where Agatha could work. It would mean she would have a home to return to when she came back, but she knew the constant leaving would hurt her greatly.

Her child, who she wanted more than anything. Well equal to one other person, but they would hopefully come part in parcel.

She had worked to make herself worthy of the mantel she had inherited and had always hired the children of friends at the lowest levels, forcing  them to work for what they wanted. It may seem harsh, but it was fair.

The boy frowned. “Am I falling behind?”

“No, not at all! It’s just I often do a lot of travelling over the summer months, which means things need to be kept afloat here, there and everywhere. I figured I’d offer you a helping hand.”

Billy smiled. “That would be great. Is it one of the interns or…”

“No, no. I have someone in mind. I will have her contact you soon and we can begin the hiring process.”

can you please give harper this and ask her to get in touch as soon as possible

Someday, she would have to sit in the back of one of her lectures, though she’d likely be too busy staring to take any of the information in. How any of her students got any work done, she would never know.

Her smile quickly faded when her laptop chimed, and a new email from one of her legal reps dropped into her inbox.

Dear Ms Vidal,

The plans submitted to convert the existing hotel has not only been approved, but the Mayor of Rome wishes to be involved in the restoration of the building’s original façade and internal features. The mayor’s office has requested a meeting to go over the plans and wishes you to be present. I have told them this may have to be over a video call, but it may put us in better graces if you came here in person. There are also design aspects the architects and interior designers wish to walk through with you.

I understand you are very busy, but at least few weeks in Italy would really help the project move forward. Also, the food here is pretty good, if that helps persuade you.

Hope to hear from you soon,

Matthew Murdock

She knew she had to go.

This project was an important one, and it had all been put off long enough. There was no question she had to head to Rome as soon as possible. Even though she had just met Agatha, and they seemed to be in a pretty good place. A place where they were finally getting to know each other, and she had to fucking leave.

perfect see you then

She was just in her work clothes, but Rio was a charmer, or she had a thing for women in blazers.

The waitress nodded and headed off.

Agatha laughed with her before shrugging. “I’m fuelled by coffee these days.”

She honestly couldn’t remember the last night she woke up truly refreshed. Perhaps it had never happened. The years she lived with her mother were filled with torment, and the years after were spent with regret. Her body had likely forgotten how to rest or was never taught to do so in the first place.

Rome was no doubt a beautiful city. 

For a long time, Rio hadn’t understood why her father never opened a hotel there. After all, it was a huge European capital with millions of visitors a year, and it wasn’t like they didn’t already have hotels in Florence, Venice, and Naples. After those, Rome should have been a no-brainer. Then, as she began to look into opening a hotel there herself, she realized why.

The hotel had to capture the heart of the city, embrace its history and culture. Rio had a clear vision of what she wanted, and it had taken her years to finally find the right foundations to make it a reality.

Rome. The unconquerable territory about to be finally brandish the Vidal name. A city of beauty and art and fucking good food.

She missed her like the moon missed the sun, and the waves missed the shore. She missed her so deeply sometimes she could hardly think, hardly breathe. She missed her…yet there wasn’t much she could do about it.

She wore a long dress with a pattern of blacks, greens and whites. Tropical, but subtle. And Rio particularly liked how low Agatha had left the buttons open.

When they made it to the hotel dining room, Rio had to give her friends credit. It was a beautiful set-up. Everything a standard white, with dark wooden chairs, the décor simple but leaning to the gorgeous location, all tying together with a large window that looked out onto the sea. Close to perfection.

They were led to their table and given the menus for the evening. Rio was pleased to see some vegetarian options, and everyone seemed happy enough. Well, all except for Agatha.

Agatha was quiet. Uncharacteristically so. Sure she added to the conversation every so often, but she seemed…distant. Lost in her thoughts. A hand.

Agatha’s hand.

…Rio’s phone buzzed in her bag.

No, this couldn’t be happening. Not now.

A day without Rio.

It was crazy, Agatha knew. A whirlwind trip to Rome with the woman she wanted so damn badly. Yet she’d already flown to fucking Sicily.

How would Rome make any difference?

Rio sat in her office, trying to read through the latest report on the progress for Rome. Honey had sent it over so it would be there when she woke up. She could hear Agatha’s voice in her head stating she was making an effort to make herself seem helpful, which was likely true. Still, she decided to ignore it, and thanked Honey for completing it and told her she would report back with a review.

Or she would if she could concentrate, which seemed like a big ask considering she’d read the same sentence five times.

She missed Agatha.

It was stupid, really. They needed time apart. To work, to socialize, to have their own time. Still, she wasn’t used to it and so far, she hated it.

A knock on her door broke her out of her misery, and she smiled as Billy walked in, iPad in hand.

“Hey Billy, what’s up?”

“The front desk called up. You have a walk-in.”

“A walk-in?” Rio frowned. “Who?”

“She said she knows you.” Billy checked his iPad. “A Ms Jennifer Kale?”

Rio’s eyebrows raised. “Really? Send her up.”

“So you do know her?”

“She’s a friend,” Rio assured, before wondering. “Is she alone?”

“Seems so.” Billy stepped back towards the door. “I’ll greet her at the elevator.”

Rio gave him a grateful smile to hide her disappointment. For a second she had hoped Alice was with her. That she had brought Jen along for support so she could apologize.

She loved Agatha and she’d always stand by her. She would never stand to anyone putting her down or fuelling cruel gossip. Still, she missed her best friend. She missed able to call her. She missed her laughter and her council. She missed Alice Wu Gulliver so much it made her sick, but she was also infuriated by what she said. How quickly she was to think the worst of the woman she loved, and how she hadn’t trusted her judgement, instead choosing to listen to rumours from a girl she barely knew.

Yet she knew that if Alice apologised, she’d forgive her in a heartbeat.

The door to her office opened once more, and Jen stepped inside, dressed in a hot pink pantsuit. Rio got up and greeted her with a hug.

“It’s good to see you. How long have you been back?”

“Just under a week,” Jen admitted. “Lilia and I didn’t want to bother you and Agatha. We knew you’d both be, erm, acclimatising.”

Rio chuckled as she moved to sit back at her desk. “Can I get you anything? Water? Tea? Coffee? Snacks?”

“I’m fine,” Jen assured as she sat opposite her. “As you’ve probably guessed, this isn’t just a social call.”

Rio nodded. “And since you came to speak to me here on the exact day Agatha went back to work, I’m guessing this is about Alice.”

Jen laughed. “You don’t miss a trick do you.”

“Nope. So, what’s up? Is Alice okay?”

“She’s fine,” Jen assured. “We’re…we’re talking again.”

“Right…”

“I called her to give her shit for what she said about Agatha. I told her it wasn’t true and she did listen. Then we just started catching up and…we’re not together again. We’ve only slept together once since.”

Rio grimaced. “Okay…”

“And she hasn’t totally changed her mind on Agatha, but she can see why Ellie Bishop’s spawn isn’t exactly a reliable source.”

“She should have known that straight away,” Rio countered and Jen held up her hands.

“Hey, I agree but I can’t stay mad at her forever, and I know you can’t either.”

Rio looked down. Jen was right on the money there. “I want to, but I can’t condone someone believing those things about the love of my life. Alice knows I’ve waited my whole life to find her, and she’s betraying her the minute she gets the chance.”

“This has never been about Agatha,” Jen argued. “Not really. She loves you and she’s…she doesn’t want you to get hurt. Look, I know Bishop is full of shit and Alice went about things the wrong way, but her intention was never to hurt Agatha. It was to look out for you.”

Though Rio remained sceptical, she couldn’t deny Alice’s motives. Even in the wrong, her actions hadn’t been about hating Agatha. It had been out of concern and out of love.

“So what do you suggest?”

“I want to invite you and Agatha over to my place for dinner. Alice has already agreed to come, so it would be a good chance for you al to talk. I’ll play mediator, of course.”

Rio smirked. “Sure you won’t be unbiased, ref?”

Jen laughed. “Please. I call bullshit when I see it, regardless of who’s spewing it.”

Rio gasped. “Ms Kale, I thought you were prim and proper!”

 Jen rolled her eyes. “You’ve been spending too much time with Agatha. So, I’ll be expecting you both about seven?”

“I hope so,” Rio answered. “I need to check with Agatha first. She’s the boss.”

Jen laughed again. “Rio, if you ask she’ll do it. The only person I’ve seen more down bad than you is her.”

Rio frowned as Jen left, momentarily confused by her words. She soon snapped out of it, though, and reached for her phone.

RIO

are you free to talk?

Agatha replied quickly.

AGATHA

Just left for a break. Why? What’s wrong?

Rio called her, and Agatha answered

“Rio? Are you okay? What’s happened?”

“Nothing bad,” Rio assured. “Jen’s just stopped by. She’s asked if we’ll go to her place tonight.”

“Tonight?” The displeasure was clear in Agatha’s voice. “Can’t we do it tomorrow? I’ve missed you all day. I just want to be back in our bubble.”

Rio understood her pain, but she knew this was important. “Jen’s got Alice to meet with us. We’re going to talk this out face to face.”

There was a long silence, and Rio worried. Then, she heard a defeated sigh.

“Alright, but tomorrow night you’re all mine.”

Rio smiled. “I’m always all yours, my love. Always have been, always will be.”

 

Agatha smiled to herself as she rejoined Wanda and Kingo at their table. Wanda noticed her first and smirked. “Was that Rio?”

“It was,” Agatha confirmed. “We have last-minute dinner plans.”

“Oh to be a millionaire,” Kingo said with a dreamy sigh. “Where are you going? Per Se? Gramercy Tavern?”

“Our friend’s dining room,” Agatha corrected. “There’s been a bit of a falling out between Rio and her best friend, so we’re going to all sit down and talk.”

“Really? What about?”

“Me.”

Both their eyes widened.

“Wait, her best friend doesn’t like you?” Wanda questioned and Agatha shrugged.

“She believes some things she’s heard. I’m not overly concerned.”

“Well, you should be,” Kingo countered. “If she doesn’t like you, you’re screwed.”

“What?” Agatha frowned. “No, I’m not. Rio has told her what’s what.”

“Trust me, Agatha. If you lose the best friend, you lose the relationship.”

Wanda swatted his arm. “Don’t say stuff like that!”

“It’s true!”

“It isn’t!”

Kingo held up his hands and got to his feet. “Fine, but don’t say I didn’t warn you!”

Agatha watched him go and huffed. “He has no clue what he’s talking about.”

“What else is new,” Wanda joked, before her expression turned serious. “But I would try settle things.”

“You just said…”

“I know but think of Rio. This must be hard for her.”

Agatha bowed her head. “It is.”

“Just make sure tonight goes well,” Wanda insisted. “It’ll save all of you the heartache.”

Agatha nodded, then looked past her to see Olivia walking in with her department. She caught her eye and waved, before sitting down on the other side of the room.

Wanda looked over her shoulder and spotted Olivia immediately. “And what’s the deal with that?”

“With what?”

Wanda pursed her lips. “This is me you’re talking to. I saw you both walking in together this morning. What’s going on?”

Agatha shrugged. “Olivia and I are fine. She knows about Rio. She even got us an engagement gift.”

“Really?” Wanda raised her eyebrows. “What was it?”

“Matching Moomin keychains.”

“Moomins?” Wanda stared at her disbelief. “You can’t be serious.”

“What’s wrong with the Moomins?”

“She got you a Moomin book last time she went away and you had it on your bedside table for six months.”

“Because I never got round to reading it,” Agatha lied. “Look, it’s fine. Olivia was…she was fun. Rio is so much more than that. The two don’t even compare.”

Wanda stared at her for a moment before relenting. “Fine, but don’t mess this up for yourself, Agatha.”

“I won’t,” she insisted. “This is different, Wanda. I can’t describe it. The way Rio makes me feel is unlike anything I’ve every experienced. Like right now pretty much all I care about it getting back to her. Being away from her hurts. Like physically hurts. So if you have any more comments…”

Wanda held up her hands. “Okay, okay, I get it.”

“Good,” Agatha huffed. “I’m sick of having to defend my relationship at every turn. Rio isn’t the only one invested, you know.”

Wanda gave her a fond smile. “I’m glad you finally have someone to fight for rather than against.”

“I’d defend my godsons until my dying breath,” Agatha reminded her, and Wanda laughed.

“Oh I have no doubt.”

Once all their meetings were finally done, Agatha called Rio and soon enough her fiancée’s car was waiting in the exact spot it had dropped her off.

Rio practically leaped out of the car, engulfing her in a hug. “I missed you so much!”

“Me too.” Agatha kissed her deeply. “Home? We could squeeze in some alone time before we have to get ready for dinner.”

Rio grinned and helped her into the car. “My darling, your wish is my command.”

 

After spending two hours wrapped up in bed sheets (and themselves), Rio reluctantly buttoned up her dress shirt and looked at herself in Agatha’s mirror. She loved wearing suits. They made her feel powerful, invincible, and she looked pretty damn hot too.

The bathroom door opened and Agatha wandered out in a simple black dress and light make up. Absolutely perfect and absolutely gorgeous. Rio couldn’t help but stare.

“You look unreal.”

“Why thank you, my love.” Agatha kissed her cheek. “You look handsome.”

“Thank you.” Rio gave her a quick peck on the cheek. “You ready?”

“Whenever you are.”

Rio finished up her hair and sprayed on some cologne. Even though it was just a dinner between friends, she wanted to look good for Agatha. As every dinner, no matter how casual, was a date in her eyes.

When she was done, she turned to Agatha and smiled. “All done.”

“Perfect, my love.” Agatha went to reach for her small clutch, before her hand instead grasped her discarded work bag. “Hey, I have something for you.”

“You do?” Rio watched as Agatha rummaged through the bag before pulling out a small paper bag. She reached into it and retrieved something that gleamed silver. “My friend at work got us matching keychains.”

“Oh, that’s sweet.” Rio took the keychain with a smile, only for it to falter. “Moomins?”

“Yeah, she was in Sweden. She picked them up at the airport.”

Rio turned it over in her palm. “Do you like the Moomins?”

“Not particularly,” Agatha admitted. “They’re cute though, right?”

Rio nodded. “Very.”

“I was thinking maybe you could put these on them.” Agatha rummaged through her bedside cabinet before pulling out a single set of keys. “Seeing as we’re spending a lot of our time here at the moment, which I don’t quite understand when you have a huge penthouse empty across town.”

“I still go to see Victoria,” Rio argued, but accepted the keys like they were priceless treasure. “You know, that corner of your living room would be perfect for a...”

“Victoria is coming nowhere near this apartment,” Agatha said firmly. “Now get that blazer on, Vidal. We have a dinner to get to.”

Rio shrugged on her jacket before taking another look at the fresh keychain in her hand. She decided it was best not to think too much into it and shoved it in her pocket before following Agatha out of the apartment.

After all, she had a friendship to salvage.

Chapter 22

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! sorry for the wait! hope you enjoy!

Agatha rang the doorbell for Jen’s penthouse, hearing the sound echo within.

She turned back to look at her fiancée, who stood quietly behind her with her arms crossed. “This is going to be chaos, you know that right?”

“I know,” Rio replied. “But I guess it’s necessary.”

The door opened to reveal Lilia in a bejewelled gown. Agatha knew her godmother never gave up the chance to get dressed up, and it seemed that night was no exception.

“Ah, here you both are! Jen’s been waiting!”

“Want are you doing here?” Agatha questioned.

“Jen called me and I couldn’t resist!” Lilia admitted, before looking past her to Rio. “And don’t you worry. Alice invited one of your friends to balance it out.”

Agatha saw Rio’s eyes widen. “Wait, which friend?”

They headed inside and sure enough, Lilia had perched herself in the main armchair, a glass of wine in her hand. Alice stood by the window with her back to them, looking out of the window across the city, and beside her stood a blonde woman dressed in cargos and a cropped white vest.

She looked over and grinned. “Rio Vidal!”

Agatha heard Rio sigh. “I should have known.”

The woman moved over and pulled Rio into a hug, picking her up off the ground. “I’ve missed you!”

“I missed you too, now put me down!”

The woman put Rio back on her feet. “Sorry, but it’s been so long. And now you’re fucking engaged!”

“Yes, no thanks to you,” Rio sassed, before looking to Agatha. “Babe, this is Carol.”

Carol. Agatha thought for a minute before it clicked.

She folded her arms. “So this is the genius who told you to buy me Cartier?”

“I didn’t specifically say Cartier, but I suppose I’m still guilty,” Carol admitted, but grinned anyway. She shook Agatha’s hand before frowning. “Are you a member at Soho House?”

Agatha scoffed. “Absolutely not.”

“Huh.” Carol tilted her head. “I’m sure I recognize you from somewhere.”

“I sent you our engagement pictures, dumbass,” Rio joked and Carol shrugged it off.

“Well, it’s nice to meet you finally.”

Agatha smiled, relieved that at least one of Rio’s friends was being nice to her.

Alice hadn’t turned to look at them, and Agatha watched as Jen stormed over to her. A few raised whispers were exchanged, before Alice huffed and finally faced the group. She gave them a weary look before moving to sit near Lilia, avoiding all their gazes.

“Right, dinner won’t be much longer,” Jen assured. “Does anyone want any wine?”

Agatha laughed. “I’d like a bucket full.”

She followed Jen through to the kitchen, and as soon as the door shut behind them, Agatha sighed.

“This is already unbearable.”

“It’ll be fine,” Jen assured. “Once we’re sat down for dinner, we’ll be able to talk this out.”

“And if we can’t?”

Jen didn’t respond. She opened a cupboard and pulled out a large wine glass. “This bucket enough for you?”

Agatha took it gladly. “Thanks.”

“Just let them hash it out,” Jen encouraged. “And try not to antagonize anyone.”

“Why would I…” Jen gave her a pointed look, and Agatha held up her hands. “Fine I’ll be on my best behaviour.”

Jen poured her some wine. “I need to finish dinner. You can either help me or go back out there.”

Agatha elected to leave and headed back into the lion’s den.

Rio had sat down on the couch, talking to Lilia and Carol. Alice had also sat down beside Carol, her eyes following Agatha as she moved to sit with her fiancée. The moment she sat down, Rio put her arm around her and kissed the side of her head.

“Everything okay, my love?”

Agatha nodded. “Jen is just finishing up dinner.”

“And I see you’ve got your wine.” Rio nodded to the large glass with an amused smirk.

“I did,” Agatha replied. “Think I’m going to need it.”

“You know, Agatha,” Carol spoke up. “I swear I know you from somewhere.”

“Perhaps you’ve seen each other at a function?” Lilia suggested. “My goddaughter usually makes quite the impression.”

Agatha shot her godmother a warning look.

“She did with me,” Rio said with a foolish grin. “The moment I saw her, she became the centre of my world.”

Agatha smiled and reached for her hand, giving it a gentle squeeze. “You made quite the impression on me too, my love.”

Carol laughed. “Yeah, you were wondering ‘who’s this loser?’”

“Shut up, Danvers,” Rio huffed. “Let us have our moment.”

Carol rolled her eyes. “Fine. I’ll save it for the wedding.”

Alice clicked her tongue, and when Agatha met her gaze, she was met with a sharp glare.

Agatha sighed. This was going to be a long night.

 

Jen had put a patisserie board together for their first course, and Lilia and Carol had tucked in eagerly. 

“This reminds me of a little restaurant tucked away near my favourite ski resort in the French alps,” Lilia commented. “It’s divine.”

“You ski?” Carol questioned, and Lilia laughed. 

“No but I enjoy the lodge.”

“Sometimes a bit too much,” Agatha commented.

“And do you ski?” Carol asked. 

Agatha shook her head. “I have before, but not for a while.”

“Then we should go!” Carol declared. “All of us. It’ll be fun!”

“Yeah,” Alice mumbled. “So much fun.”

Rio gave her a warning look, but Alice just shrugged in response. 

Jen got to her feet. “Well, is everyone ready for the first course?”

“Oh yes,” Lilia replied. “It smells divine.”

Jen left the table, which fell into an uncomfortable silence. Rio stole a glance at Alice. Their eyes met for an instant, before her once closest friend quickly looked away. 

Her heart hurt. Rio had dreamed of this for so long. To have her friends and the love of her life around her, enjoying an evening all together. Only this had become more of a nightmare. 

Jen brought out a vegetarian ragu that was beyond divine. It was as they tucked in that their host then kicked started the purpose of their gathering. 

“Right, let’s begin by sharing our feelings on the engagement. I for one am happy for my friends.”

“Me too,” Carol added with a wink. “Been a long time coming.”

“And I’m happy that my goddaughter has found someone who clearly adores her.”

Rio grinned. “I don’t think adore even covers it.”

Agatha smiled, a blush pinking her cheeks. 

“Alice?” Jen questioned. “Your thoughts?”

Alice looked down at her plate, pushing her food with her folk. 

Jen cleared her throat, and Alice reluctantly looked up. “I-I’m happy Rio is happy.”

Well, that was something, right?

“Care to add anything else?” Jen pressed. 

Alice remained silent for a moment before putting down her folk. “Look, I know I’m being seen as the bad guy here, but you need to see this from my point of view.”

Rio saw Agatha fold her arms. “And what view is that?”

Alice shot Agatha a glare. “That this is all very suspicious.”

“Suspicious?” Rio questioned. “What? Because you heard some stupid rumour?”

“No. It’s because this is all very convenient.”

“Convenient? What’s that supposed to mean?”

“That she had no interest in you until you whisked her off to Rome and showed her around your lakeside villa. Then within a couple of weeks you’re fucking engaged?! Do you realize how that looks?”

“It’s not like that,” Rio insisted. “Agatha doesn’t like my money.”

Alice scoffed. “Oh please.”

“I don’t!” Agatha snapped, but even Carol looked dubious. 

“There’s no shame in enjoying it,” she assured. “As long as it’s not the reason you’re together.”

Rio barely had time to consider Carol’s point before Agatha shot it down. 

“I don’t want her money. In fact, her money is why it took so long for this to happen. I’ve had that kind of money, and I was more miserable with it than without it.” 

“I find that hard to believe,” Alice countered, and Rio could see Carol also remained unconvinced. Her, Jen and Lilia knew Agatha’s truth, and if they knew too, this would be no question.

“It’s the truth,” Agatha insisted. “I don’t want to be in this world again, and luckily your gossiping friends have proven exactly why. Annoyingly, I can be happy without the money, but now I can’t be happy without Rio. It took me a while to accept my feelings, but now I have, I have accepted that I can’t have it both ways. Rio is worth all of this, but she doesn’t deserve her best friend being a bitch about it.”

“I’m protecting her!” Alice snapped back. 

“She doesn’t need protecting from me! I love her!”

Alice folded her arms. “Alright then. Look me in the eye and tell me you didn’t kill your mother.”

Rio felt Agatha tense, and she quickly reached for her hand. 

“She didn’t,” Lilia insisted. “You have no idea what happened. None of you do.”

“Then explain it to me,” Alice countered. “Tell me the ‘truth’.”

Silence fell across the room, eyes shifting between each other sheepishly. Until eventually Agatha cleared her throat sharply. 

“My mother fell down the stairs. The paramedics couldn’t do anything.”

“So she fell?”

“More like tumbled,” Agatha countered. “The stairs were marble. Very impractical.”

Alice stared at her in disbelief. “She died because the stairs were impractical. What the fuck is wrong with you?!”

“What do you want me to do? Cry?”

“I’d expect you not to joke about it.”

“Well sorry to disappoint.”

Rio put her head in her hands. This was a nightmare.

“Alice,” Jen spoke up. “Agatha doesn’t always express her emotions…”

“I don’t need you sticking up for me, Kale.” Agatha got to her feet. “I’ll lay things out simply for you all. My mom was a bitch and she died. She fell down the stairs. Am I sad about it? Not at all. In fact, it was the best thing that ever happened to me, but she fell down the stairs. No big conspiracy. Now, if you’ll excuse me, I need something stronger than wine.”

Rio watched her fiancée leave and moved to follow her before Lilia put a handout to stop her.

“Let me,” her future (god)mother-in-law insisted. “I’ve dealt with this for long enough.”

Lilia followed Agatha out of the room, leaving Rio to hold down the fort.

“Alice, Agatha didn’t have a good childhood. I know all three of our lives have been marked by tragedy, but it’s different for her than for us. Her mother was cruel, and it took her dying for her to finally be free. The money means nothing.”

Alice pursed her lips, avoiding Rio’s gaze. “I want you to be safe and happy.”

“I am,” Rio insisted. “The only person making me unhappy right now is you!”

“I don’t mean to! I just find this all too good to be true!”

Rio’s heart sank further, tears stinging her eyes. “Is it really that hard to believe that someone loves me?”

Alice’s eyes widened. “No, of course not! I just find it…” Her shoulders slumped. “Rio, I’ve known you a long time. You’re of course beautiful…”

Jen cleared her throat and Alice rolled her eyes. “Babe, she’s like my sister.”

Jen sighed. “Fine. Continue.”

“You’re beautiful, and kind, and generous, but you’re also a little…naïve at times. You see the best in everyone, but it sometimes means you don’t realise people’s true intentions.”

Rio considered this. She recalled when she first took Agatha to Rome, how she’d missed Honey’s flirtations for months when Agatha spotted it almost instantly. How many times had this happened without her realising. Was she truly that oblivious?

“I can understand that, but you don’t have to worry in this case.”

“How can I not?” Alice argued. “From the moment you saw her, you’ve had hearts in your eyes, and I’m worried it’s blinding you.”

“I’m not blind. I know Agatha has her…quirks, but you can’t choose who you fall in love with, and even if I could, I wouldn’t change my mind. Agatha is the only woman I’ve ever had feels for, or even looked at in that way…”

“Not true,” Carol interjected.

“What do you mean?” Rio questioned.

“Agatha isn’t the only woman and you damn well know it.”

Rio frowned. “I’ve never loved anyone in the way I love Agatha.”

“That’s not what you said. You said you’ve never looked at another woman other than her and that’s an outright lie. You worked out you were gay before we met.”

“I can notice that other women are beautiful,” Rio argued. “That just makes me human. This is different.”

“And what about Hela when you were all cosy during that skiing trip?” Carol questioned. “I know you didn’t go all the way, but…”

“I was curious!” Rio quickly defended herself. “It was never…it wasn’t…”

“And let’s not forget party girl,” Alice interjected, and Carol clicked her fingers.

“Yes! She spent six months sulking because she thought she’d fumbled the love of her life.”

Rio put her head in her hands. She hated thinking about that night. Not that she was precious about the idea of virginity, but she did wish she could erase it. That her first time was the one she could remember. With Agatha on the edge of Lake Como. That it was actually something meaningful.

“You two are twisting her words,” Jen finally butted in. “It doesn’t matter what women have existed in Rio’s past, and you don’t need to overanalyse everything. Rio is grown, and if her and Agatha are happy, that should be enough.”

Rio looked to Alice hopefully, but her best friend simply got to her feet and walked out of the room. They all watched her leave, Jen seemingly divided, but they all stayed seated. All stayed quiet…until Carol eventually spoke up again.

“You know, it’s really bugging me where I know Agatha from.”

Rio dropped her head to the table. She wanted to book a direct flight back to Italy pronto.

 

Agatha raided through Jen’s pantry, displeased with each bottle she picked up. She heard the kitchen door open. “Jen, where’s your hard liquor?”

“Not Jen.”

Agatha looked over her shoulder and saw Lilia stood behind her. Oh great. A serious talk. She quickly turned her attention back to the cupboard.

“Jen has nothing but fancy wine. Not even a bottle of Jack.”

 

“Agatha…”

“That’s my name.”

“You need to tell the whole story.”

Agatha laughed. “Absolutely not.”

“Agatha…”

“No, Lilia. I’m not dragging all that up again. I want to move on with my life, and I’d been doing a good job of it until you dragged me to that fucking fundraiser. Now I’m in love with one of the richest women in the world and her friends are assholes.”

“Alice isn’t an asshole,” Lilia assured. “And you have nothing to be ashamed of.”

“Then I don’t have to explain myself,” Agatha countered, before a bottle caught her eye. “Aha!”

“Agatha…”

Agatha held up the bottle for her godmother to see. “Good old tequila.”

“Agatha!” Lilia snapped. “Enough!”

Suddenly she was a teenager again, still pushing against boundaries that no longer existed. She looked to Lilia, the only parental figure she’d ever had, and reluctantly set the tequila aside.

“I didn’t want any of this,” she admitted. “Do any of you get that? I-I liked Rio before Italy, but I pushed her away because I didn’t want this fucking mess again. But Rio had to make me fall head over heels in love with her and I was stupid enough to think that everything would be fine while we were thousands of miles away. Now I can’t go back because the thought of living without her makes my heart hurt so I guess I’m miserable either way.”

“Have you told Rio this?”

“She knows I don’t like this, and she’s been good about it, but what more can she do? Alice is like family to her. I can see this is making her miserable.”

Lilia reached out and rubbed her arm. They weren’t huggers, but Agatha appreciated the act. “Everything will be alright.”

“How can you possibly know that?”

“Because I do.”

“How reassuring.”

“Just trust me,” Lilia assured. “It’ll all be okay.”

Agatha decided to relent. “I hope you’re right.”

Lilia smiled. “You really love her, don’t you?”

“I do,” Agatha admitted. “It took me a while to catch up, but I think I understand what it was like for Rio when we met. Now I look at her and…I don’t think I’ve ever loved anything as much as I love her. No offense.”

Lilia chuckled. “Trust me, I’m delighted. All I’ve ever wanted was for you to be happy.”

Agatha then narrowed her eyes. “Tell anyone and I’ll tell them about your wild weekend in Vienna.”

Lilia laughed and held a hand over her heart. “Don’t worry, Agatha. I won’t let anyone know you have feelings.”

“Good.” Agatha then reached for the tequila bottle. “Let’s seal it with a with a shot.”

Lilia chuckled and retrieved some glasses. “I know I raised you well.”

“You did,” Agatha agreed. “All my good parts come from you.”

Neither of them commented on the way their eyes glistened. After all, it was just a trick of the light.

 

Jen’s penthouse had access to a large balcony, looking out over the city, enclosed by a tall railing. Rio found Alice stood out there, staring out across the building tops as she took a drag of her cigarette.

After a moment of consideration, Rio decided to join her. “Got another one of those?”

Alice wordlessly reached into her jacket pocket and handed Rio the pack of cigarettes and her zippo lighter. She pulled one out and lit it, before giving both back.

“Thanks.”

Alice once again didn’t respond, and so they stood side by side taking drags as the last sign of the sun began to fade from the sky. Rio waited, and waited, her cigarette half finished when her best friend finally found her voice.

“I’m sorry.”

“I know,” Rio answered. “And I understand why you had your apprehensions, even if I don’t agree with all your reasoning.”

Alice turned to face her fully. “You’re the only family I have left, Rio. Sure, I have Jen, Carol, and others I can count on, but you’re different. We’ve been through so much, stood by each other through good and bad. I want you to be happy, but I also worry you’re going to get hurt.”

“I feel the same,” Rio replied honestly. “And I do appreciate you wanting to look after me, but I need to make my own decisions. I want to be with Agatha. She’s my choice.”

“I know.” Alice bowed her head. “I’m sorry for believing the rumours.”

“I’m not the person you should be apologizing to,” Rio pointed out. “Agatha has been through enough without our inner circle believing her antagonists.”

“I’m going to set Nat and Yelena straight, too,” Alice insisted. “I don’t know how it’ll go down though. Yelena is close with Kate.”

“We’ll cross that bridge another day,” Rio answered. “All that matters is that we’re okay again.”

“We are,” Alice assured. “And I’ll make things right with Agatha.”

“Good.” Rio took another drag from her cigarette. “I thought you were quitting?”

“I thought you had quit.”

Rio laughed. “Touché.”

They headed back inside and when they entered the dining room, she was relieved to see Agatha at the table, laughing with Lilia and Jen at a story Carol was telling.

“So I told the guy I was flying the plane and he looked to Fury and said ‘I thought you were the pilot?’. So fury looked him dead in the eye and said “You let me drink all this champagne when you thought I was flying the motherfucking plane?’”

Rio rolled her eyes. She’d heard that story more times that she could count. Still, it was nice to see her fiancée laugh after what had already been an eventual night.

It was Carol who looked to them first, her bright smile not faltering. “Ah. Look who it is.”

Jen’s lips pursed, Lilia’s eyes looked between them nervously, while Agatha folded her arms. Not in challenge, though it may seem so to some, but Rio knew it was in defence. As most of her I-don’t-give-a-fuck façade truly was.

Alice stepped ahead of Rio and made her way over to Agatha. “I’m sorry for believing stupid rumours. I was worried about my friend, but it seems I’ve just made things worse.”

Rio worried for a moment. As much as she adored her fiancée, she knew she wasn’t always the most…reasonable, and in this case she had more than enough cause to shun Alice’s apology. Yet, to her surprise, Agatha nodded in acceptance.

“Thank you, Alice.”

“I hope we can find a way to move past this,” Alice added. “Considering we’re pretty much family now.”

Agatha laughed nervously. “I’ve never been too good with family.”

“Hey, my mom was an unhinged rockstar who died in a hotel fire when I needed her most. Family isn’t something that comes natural to me either, but I think we can work this out.”

Alice sat back down beside Jen, who reached for her hand and squeezed it. Rio smiled and returned to her future wife’s side.

“You okay?” She asked, and Agatha nodded.

“Much better.” She gave Rio a quick kiss on the lips before quickly pulling back and frowning. “You’ve been smoking?”

“Just one.”

Agatha gave her a disapproving look. “Make sure it’s your last.”

Rio nodded. “Of course, my love.”

“Unless you’re sharing with me then that’s fine.”

Rio laughed and kissed her cheek. “You have yourself a deal.”
